Ruling on the Beard of a Slave: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for slave's beard.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding compensation for cutting a slave's beard and identify the mufta bihi position with its reasoning.

Core Idea
A slave's beard is not a free man's beard: beauty vs. service changes the compensation.

This passage addresses a nuanced issue within the Hanafi school: the compensation (diyat) for cutting a slave's beard. While a free man's beard commands full diya, the slave's beard is treated differently because the intended benefit of a slave is service, not adornment. Within the school, there is a disagreement between a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa and the established transmission (zahir al-riwaya). Understanding this ikhtilaf and its resolution sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi usul and tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What is the act being ruled upon? Cutting the beard of a slave. What is the legal question? What compensation is wajib?
The act is an injury (jinayah) on a slave.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
One position (a narration from Abu Hanifa) holds that the full price of the slave is wajib. The other (zahir al-riwaya, the view of the Sahibayn) holds that only the decrease in value (hikumat 'adl) is wajib.
The opposing school here is not another madhhab but an intra-Hanafi variant.
3
Analyze the reasoning for each position
The reasoning for the decrease-in-value position: In a free person, beauty is the purpose of the beard; in a slave, the benefit of service is the purpose, and service is unaffected by beard removal. Therefore, only the loss in market value is compensated. The full-price position may analogize to other injuries where full value is given.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) based on the intended purpose (maqsad).
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The zahir al-riwaya is the relied-upon position in the school. Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah prefers it. Thus, for fatwa, the decrease in value is wajib.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwaya is the most authoritative.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa's narration, the owner receives the full market value of the slave. Under the mufta bihi, the owner receives only the assessed decrease in value due to the beard removal.
This affects actual compensation amounts in lawsuits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مالک اور امام شافعی کا داڑھی اور سر کے بالوں کو ان پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ اور رہی غلام کی داڑھی تو نو اور میں امام ابو حنیفہ سے یہ روایت ہے کہ اس صورت میں بھی غلام کی پوری قیمت واجب ہوگی لہذا قیاس ہی صحیح نہ ہوگا البتہ ظاہر الروایہ یہ ہے کہ قیمت کا نقصان واجب ہوگا۔ تو پھر امام صاحب کی طرف سے یہ جواب ہوگا کہ آزاد میں جمال مقصود ہے اور غلام میں خدمت کی منفعت مقصود ہے جو داڑھی کٹنے کے بعد بھی موجود ہے اس لئے غلام میں نقصان قیمت واجب ہے اور آزاد میں پوری دیت۔
Malik and Imam Shafi'i's analogy of the beard and head hair to them is an analogy with a difference. As for the slave's beard, there is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that in this case also, the full price of the slave is obligatory, therefore the analogy is not correct; however, the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) is that the loss in value is obligatory. So then the response from Imam Sahib will be: In a free person, beauty is intended; in a slave, the benefit of service is intended, which remains even after the beard is cut. Therefore, for the slave, loss in value is obligatory, and for the free person, full diya.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for cutting the beard of a slave versus a free man within the Hanafi school. It begins by noting that Malik and Shafi'i analogize the beard and head hair to other body parts, but this analogy is flawed. Then it presents an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa is reported in a narration to hold that the full price (of the slave) is wajib, but the zahir al-riwaya (the established transmission) states that only the decrease in value is wajib. The commentator explains that Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that for free men, beauty is the purpose of the beard, whereas for slaves, the benefit of service is the purpose, which is unaffected by beard removal. Thus, for a free man, full diya; for a slave, only the depreciation in value.

Key Terms
حکومت عدل (hukumat 'adl): An equitable assessment of the decrease in value of a slave due to injury, not a fixed amount.
ظاہر الروایہ (zahir al-riwaya): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani containing the authoritative transmissions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the zahir al-riwaya, what is the ruling for cutting a slave's beard?
A) Full diya
B) No compensation
C) Decrease in value (hikumat 'adl)
D) Half diya

Key Takeaway
For a slave's beard, the mufta bihi is the decrease in value (hikumat 'adl), not full diya, because the purpose of a slave is service, not beauty.

Mustache Compensation: Hukumat 'Adl Due to Subordination
States the ruling that only hukumat 'adl is wajib for the mustache, supported by qiyas to the beard's sides.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mustache compensation, explain the qiyas to the beard's sides, and apply the principle of subordination (taba'iyyah) to similar cases.

Core Idea
The mustache is subordinate to the beard, so its injury incurs only equitable compensation, not full diya.

In this lesson, we examine a concise ruling from the chapter of diyat (blood money). The Hanafi school holds that if someone's mustache is cut off, the required compensation is not a fixed amount but rather an equitable estimation called hukumat 'adl. The reasoning is rooted in the principle of subordination: the mustache is considered a follower (tabi') of the beard. Understanding this ruling clarifies how Hanafi fiqh treats parts that lack a prescribed diya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What specific act is being ruled upon? (Cutting off the entire mustache). What is the hukm level and type of compensation? (hukumat 'adl is wajib).
The text says 'puri monchh' (entire mustache).
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
What proof is cited? The author states: 'because it is a follower of the beard'. This is a qiyas (analogy).
No direct Quran or hadith is cited; the evidence is rational analogy.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The mustache is subordinate to the beard. Since shaving the sides of the beard only requires hukumat 'adl, the mustache, being a part of that same system, follows the same ruling.
The illah (cause) is subordination (taba'iyyah).
4
Note the tarjih (preference)
The author says 'it is the most correct' (asahh), indicating that this is the chosen, mufta bihi position.
No disagreement is mentioned, so it is the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مونچھ میں حکومت عدل واجب ہے
قال وفى الشارب حكومة عدل وهو الأصح لانه تابع للحية فصار كبعض اطرافه ترجمہ مصنف نے فرمایا اور مونچھ میں حکومت عدل واجب ہے اور یہی اصح ہے اس لئے کہ مونچھ داڑھی کے تابع ہے پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسے داڑھی کے بعض اطراف۔ تشریح اگر کسی کی پوری مونچھ کاٹ دی تو اس صورت میں حکومت عدل ہے کیونکہ مونچھ داڑھی کے تابع ہے اور داڑھی کے اعتراف مونڈنے میں بھی حکومت عدل ہے تو مونچھ مونڈھنے میں حکومت عدل ہے۔
Hukumat 'adl is wajib in the mustache. He said: 'And regarding the mustache, hukumat 'adl (is wajib), and it is the most correct, because it is a follower of the beard, so it becomes like some of its sides.' Translation: The author said: And in the mustache, hukumat 'adl is wajib, and this is the most correct, because the mustache is subordinate to the beard, so it is like some of the sides of the beard. Explanation: If someone's entire mustache is cut, then in this case hukumat 'adl is applied, because the mustache is subordinate to the beard, and in shaving the sides of the beard, hukumat 'adl is also applied, so in shaving the mustache, hukumat 'adl is applied.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage gives the Hanafi ruling on the mustache. It states that for cutting the mustache, only hukumat 'adl (equitable compensation) is wajib, not full diya. The reason is that the mustache is considered a subordinate part of the beard (tabi' lil-lihyah). Since the beard itself, when its sides are shaved, only requires hukumat 'adl, the mustache follows the same ruling. The text confirms that this is the most correct (asahh) position.

Key Terms
حکومت عدل (hukumat 'adl): An equitable estimation of compensation by an expert, not a fixed amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling for cutting off someone's mustache?
A) Full diya
B) Hukumat 'adl
C) No compensation
D) Half diya

Key Takeaway
The mustache's compensation is hukumat 'adl because it is subordinate to the beard, following the principle that a follower takes the ruling of the followed.

Beard of a Khawaj: Three Scenarios for Compensation
Specifies when compensation is due for shaving a sparse beard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for compensation when shaving a khawaj's beard and identify the correct compensation (nothing, hukumat 'adl, or full diya) based on the quantity and connectivity of the hair.

Core Idea
Shaving a khawaj's beard may require full diya, partial compensation, or nothing — depending on whether the hair is sparse, moderate, or forms a connected beard.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies a nuanced ruling in diyat: compensation for shaving a beard depends on the nature of the hair growth. A khawaj (an elderly man with sparse facial hair) may have only a few strands, a moderate but disconnected patch, or a full connected beard. Each case carries a different legal consequence. Understanding this distinction prevents over- or under-application of diya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the passage carefully and list the three conditions of the khawaj's beard: (1) a few counted hairs on the chin, (2) more hairs on chin and cheeks but not connected, (3) connected hair forming a full beard.
The connectivity is key.
2
Understand the key terms
Define 'khawaj' (beardless man) and 'manbit' (hair root). Note that compensation applies only if the manbit is permanently ruined.
The term 'khawaj' may be unfamiliar; it refers to a man whose beard growth is naturally very sparse despite age.
3
Apply the hukm to each scenario
For scenario 1: no compensation (hair disfigures). For scenario 2: hukumat 'adl (partial compensation) because some beauty existed. For scenario 3: full diya (because beauty was present and completely lost).
Hukumat 'adl is an assessed compensation by a fair arbitrator.
4
Note the overarching condition
The passage ends by stating that diya is only wajib when the manbit is ruined. If the hair grows back, no compensation is due.
This limits the application to permanent damage.
5
Test with a concrete case
Imagine a khawaj with a few scattered hairs on his chin (not on cheeks). His beard is shaved and the roots are destroyed. Compensation?
Answer: nothing, because the hair did not beautify him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کھوسے کی داڑھی جس کی ٹھوڑی پر چند بال تھے مونڈ دی تو کچھ واجب نہیں

ولحية الكوسج ان كان على ذقنه شعرات معدودة فلا شئ فى حلقة لان وجوده يشينه ولا يزينه وان كان اكثر من ذالك وكان على الخد والذقن جميعا لكنه غير متصل ففيه حكومة عدل لان فيه بعض الجمال وان كان متصلا ففيه كمال الدية لانه ليس بكوسج وفيه معنى الجمال

ترجمہ اور کھوے کی داڑھی اگر اس کی ٹھوڑی پر چند بال ہوں تو اس کے مونڈنے میں کچھ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس کا وجوب اس کو عیب دار کرے گا اور مزین نہیں کرے گا اور اگر اس سے زیادہ ہوں اور گال اور ٹھوڑی دونوں پر ہوں لیکن متصل نہ ہوں تو اس میں حکومت عدل ہے اس لئے کہ اس میں کچھ جمال ہے اگر متصل ہوں تو اس میں پوری دیت ہے اس لئے یہ کھو سا نہیں ہے اور اس میں جمال کے معنی ہیں ۔ تشریح کھو سا اس شخص کو کہتے ہیں جس کے داڑھی یعنی داڑھی کا زمانہ آگیا اور بوڑھا ہو گیا لیکن داڑھی نہیں آئی جیسے کچھ لوگ ایسے ہوتے ہیں تو اس کی تین صورتیں ہیں۔ - اس کی ٹھوڑی پر گنے اپنے بال ہوں تو اس کے رہنے سے کچھ جمال نہ ہوگا بلکہ اور خراب لگے گا لہذا اس کے مونڈنے میں کچھ واجب
-1
نہ ہوگا۔
کچھ زیادہ ہیں یعنی ٹھوڑی پر بھی ہیں اور رخسار پر بھی لیکن متصل نہیں ہیں تو اس میں حکومت عدل واجب ہے کیونکہ اس میں کچھ جمال تھا جو فوت ہو گیا ہے۔ بال کچھ زیادہ ہیں اور تل بھی ہیں تو ان کے مونڈنے میں پوری دیت واجب ہوگی کیونکہ ا یہ کھو انہیں رہا اور اس میں جمال تھا

جو حالق نے ختم کر دیا ہے۔ ان تمام مذکورہ صورتوں میں دیت تب واجب ہے کہ منبت ( داڑھی اگنے کی جگہ ) خراب ہو جائے
Beard of the khawaj (beardless man) whose chin had a few hairs was shaved: nothing is wajib. And the beard of the khawaj: if on his chin there are counted hairs, then nothing in shaving it, because its existence disfigures him and does not beautify him. And if it is more than that, and it is on both the cheek and the chin but not connected, then in it is hukumat 'adl, because there is some beauty in it. And if it is connected, then in it is full diya, because he is not a khawaj and in it is the meaning of beauty. Translation: And the beard of the khawaj: if his chin has a few hairs, then in shaving it there is nothing, because its existence makes him defective and does not beautify. And if there are more than that, and they are on both cheek and chin but not connected, then in it is hukumat 'adl, because there is some beauty in it. And if they are connected, then in it is full diya, because this is not a khawaj and in it are the meanings of beauty. Explanation: Khawaj is said for a person whose beard time has come and he has grown old, but beard did not come, like some people are. So his three scenarios: 1) His chin has counted hairs, so their existence gives no beauty, rather looks worse, so in shaving it, nothing is wajib. 2) There are more, i.e., on the chin and on the cheeks but not connected, so in it hukumat 'adl is wajib, because there was some beauty that has been lost. 3) The hairs are more and they are also connected, so in shaving them full diya is wajib, because this is not a khawaj and there was beauty that the barber has destroyed. In all these mentioned cases, diya is only wajib when the manbit (place of hair growth) is ruined.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage addresses the beard of a khawaj, a man who is old but has scanty facial hair. It distinguishes three scenarios based on the quantity and connectedness of the hair. If only a few scattered hairs exist, their removal incurs no compensation because their presence actually makes the person look worse (yushinuhu). If there is a moderate amount covering the chin and cheeks but not connected, hukumat 'adl is wajib because some beauty (jamal) existed and was lost. If the hair is connected and forms a full beard, even if the person is considered a khawaj, full diya is wajib because the person is not truly a khawaj (the beard is normal). The concluding line emphasizes that in all cases, compensation is only due if the hair root (manbit) is permanently ruined.

Key Terms
كوسج (khawaj): A man who is old but has sparse or light beard growth.
منبت (manbit): The place where hair grows, specifically the root area of the beard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a khawaj has a few detached hairs on his chin and cheeks, what compensation is due for shaving them?
A) Full diya
B) Hukumat 'adl
C) No compensation
D) Half diya

Key Takeaway
Compensation for shaving a khawaj's beard hinges on whether the hair adds beauty: if sparse, no compensation; if moderate but disconnected, partial; if connected, full diya.

Beard Removal: Regrowth and White Hair Compensation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for beard regrowth color change

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation when a shaved beard regrows, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding white regrowth.

Core Idea
Full regrowth cancels diya; white regrowth triggers a dispute over beauty versus disfigurement.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical question: what if a beard is forcibly shaved and then regrows? The answer distinguishes between normal regrowth (no compensation) and white regrowth (disputed). The core of the ruling lies in whether the injury's effect remains, and within the Hanafi school, the two Sahibayn differ from Abu Hanifa on the treatment of white hair. Let us walk through the legal reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline ruling
The passage first states that if the hair grows back exactly as before, nothing is wajib because the effect of the injury is gone. However, the perpetrator is disciplined (ta'zir) for committing an unlawful act.
This is the default: no financial compensation (diya or hukumat) when normal regrowth occurs.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
The dispute arises when the beard regrows white. Abu Hanifa's view is that for a free man, no compensation is due because white hair increases beauty; for a slave, hukumat 'adl is due because it decreases value. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that hukumat 'adl is wajib for both free and slave.
The key difference is the assessment of white hair: beautifying or disfiguring?
3
Analyze the reasoning behind each view
Abu Hanifa considers white hair in its natural place as beautifying, but only for a free man. The Sahibayn argue that white hair out of its proper time (i.e., in a young man) is disfiguring, regardless of free or slave status.
The reasoning is based on custom and aesthetic judgment, not direct textual evidence.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states that the majority (jumhur) of scholars adopt the view of the Sahibayn, making hukumat 'adl wajib in both cases. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
Despite Abu Hanifa's ijtihad, the later school preference shifted to the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا كله اذا فسد المنبت فان نبتت حتى استوى كما كان لا يجب شئ لانه لم يبق اثر الجناية ويؤدب على ارتكابه مالا يحل وان نبتت بيضاء فعن ابي حنيفة انه لا يجب شئ فى الحر لانه يزيده جمالا وفي العبد تجب حكومة عدل لانه ينقص قيمته وعندهما تجب حكومة عدل لانه فى غير اوانه يشينه ولا يزينه ويستوى العمد والخطأ على هذا الجمهور

ترجمہ اور یہ سب گفتگو جب ہے جب کہ منبت فاسد ہو جائے پس اگر داڑھی اگ جائے یہاں تک کہ جیسی تھی ویسی ہو جائے تو کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ جنایت کا اثر باقی نہیں رہا اور اس کی تادیب کی جائے گی اس کے ارتکاب کرنے کی وجہ سے ایسی چیز کا جو حلال نہیں ہے اور اگر سفید داڑھی اگی تو ابوحنیفہ سے منقول ہے کہ آزاد میں کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ یہ اس کا جمال بڑھاتی ہے اور غلام میں حکومت عدل واجب ہے اس لئے کہ یہ اس کی قیمت کو گھٹاتی ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک حکومت عدل واجب ہے اس لئے کہ سفید داڑھی بے وقت عیب دار کرتی ہے اور مزین نہیں کرتی اور اس میں عمد اور خطا دونوں برابر ہیں ، جمہور اسی تحقیق پر ہیں۔ تشریح مذکورہ تمام صورتوں میں دیت تب واجب ہوگی کہ پھر داڑھی وغیرہ نہ اُگے اور منبت خراب ہو جائے اور اگر اگ جائے تو کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ جنایت کا اثر باقی نہیں رہا۔ البتہ اس کے نام فعل کا ارتکاب کرنے کی وجہ سے اس کی تعزیر کی جائے گی، اور اگر حلاق کے بعد سفید داڑھی اُگے تو اگر آزاد ہو تو کچھ واجب نہیں کیونکہ سفید داڑھی آزاد کے جمال کو بڑھاتی ہے اور اگر غلام ہو تو حکومت عدل ہے اس لئے کہ غلام کی داڑھی سفید ہونے سے اس کی قیمت گھٹ جائے گی یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں حکومت عدل واجب ہے کیونکہ داڑھی کا اپنے وقت پر سفید ہونا باعث زینت و جمال ہے اور بے وقت خراب ہوتی ہے، پھر اس تفصیل میں عمداً اور خطاء مونڈ نا دونوں کا حکم ایک ہے جمہور علما ء کا یہی قول ہے۔
And all this is when the manbit (root) is ruined. So if it grows back until it is as before, nothing is wajib, because the effect of the injury does not remain, and he is disciplined for committing what is unlawful. And if it grows white, from Abu Hanifa it is narrated that nothing is wajib for the free person, because it increases his beauty, and in the slave, hukumat 'adl is wajib, because it decreases his value. And according to the two (Sahibayn), hukumat 'adl is wajib in both, because white beard out of season disfigures and does not beautify. Intentional and mistaken are equal in this, according to the majority. Translation: And all this discussion applies when the manbit is ruined. So if the beard grows back until it is as before, nothing is wajib, because the effect of the injury does not remain, but he should be disciplined for committing what is unlawful. And if white beard grows, it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that in a free person, nothing is wajib, because it increases his beauty; and in a slave, hukumat 'adl is wajib, because it decreases his value. And according to Sahibayn, hukumat 'adl is wajib in both, because white beard out of season is disfiguring and not beautifying. And in this, intentional and mistake are equal; the majority (jumhur) are on this verification. Explanation: In all the mentioned cases, diya is only wajib if the beard etc. does not grow back and the manbit is ruined. If it grows back, nothing is wajib, because the effect of the injury remains? Actually 'does not remain'? It says 'if it grows back, nothing is wajib because the effect of the injury does not remain.' He is disciplined for committing a forbidden act. Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage discusses two critical conditions: hair regrowth and color change. First, if the hair regrows completely to its original state, no diya is owed because the harm is undone; however, the perpetrator is punished (ta'zir) for committing an unlawful act. Second, if the hair regrows white, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. Abu Hanifa holds that for a free man, no compensation is due because white hair is considered beautifying for an older man, while for a slave, hukumat 'adl is due because it decreases his market value. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that hukumat 'adl is wajib in both cases, because white hair out of its natural season (i.e., in a young man) is disfiguring. The text ends by stating that the jumhur (majority) are on the latter view, and that intent and accident are treated the same in this ruling.

Key Terms
منبت (manbit): The place of hair growth, specifically the root of the beard.
عمد وخطا (amd wa khata): Intentional and mistaken acts; both are treated equally in diyat for beard removal.
حكومة عدل (hukumat 'adl): Arbitration by a fair assessor to determine the amount of compensation for an injury not covered by fixed diya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
If a forcibly shaved beard regrows white, the mufta bihi position requires hukumat 'adl for both free and slave, as the majority consider it disfiguring when out of season.

Compensation for Eyebrows: Diya vs Hukumat 'Adl
States Hanafi ruling and mentions inter-madhhab disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on diya for eyebrows, identify the opposing Maliki/Shafi'i position, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) between fixed compensation and equitable assessment.

Core Idea
Eyebrows carry full diya in the Hanafi school, unlike beard which is assessed equitably by opponents.

This lesson examines a specific inter-madhhab dispute concerning compensation for removal of eyebrows. While the Hanafi school prescribes a fixed diya (full for both, half for one) based on the principle of fixed compensation for paired body parts, the Maliki and Shafi'i schools apply hukumat 'adl (equitable assessment) similar to their ruling on the beard. Understanding this difference clarifies the Hanafi methodology of categorizing body parts for diyat.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school rules for eyebrows: full diya for both, half diya for one.
Diya is the fixed blood money, not discretionary compensation.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Which schools oppose the Hanafi view and what is their position? Maliki and Shafi'i hold that hukumat 'adl (equitable compensation) is wajib, following their reasoning on the beard.
'Hukumat 'adl means the judge assesses a fair amount based on the injury and victim's status.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The text refers to the earlier beard discussion for the detailed proofs of both sides. In that discussion, the opponents argue that facial hair like beard and eyebrows are not among the body parts with a fixed diya in the Quran or Sunnah, so general principles of equity apply.
This reference shows the interconnectedness of fiqh rulings on related body parts.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school likely argues that eyebrows, like other paired organs (e.g., eyes, ears), have a fixed diya because they are well-defined and integral to the face. The precedent from the beard is rejected as the beard is not considered a separate fixed-organ category in their school.
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between body parts that have a specified diya in authoritative texts and those that are left to judicial discretion.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence? Under Hanafi, both eyebrows lost = 10 camels (or equivalent) for a male; one eyebrow = 5 camels. Under Maliki/Shafi'i, the amount is assessed by experts and can vary based on the victim's appearance and social standing.
Fixed diya provides certainty; hukumat 'adl aims at individual justice.

This is based on the principle that eyebrows have a fixed diya like other paired body parts. The text notes that Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i hold that only hukumat 'adl (equitable compensation) is wajib, similar to their view on the beard. The author refers to the earlier discussion in the beard section for the detailed arguments of both sides.

حكومة عدل (hukumat 'adl): Equitable compensation assessed by a qualified judge, not a fixed amount.
الحاجبين (al-hajibayn): The two eyebrows.

Diyah for Beard Injury: The White Hair Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for beard injury when hair regrows white

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on diyah for regrown white beard hair and state the ruling for free and slave persons.

Core Idea
Compensation for a beard that grows back white depends on whether the hair enhances or detracts from appearance.

This passage examines a specific scenario in diyat: when a shaved beard regrows white. The ruling hinges on whether the white hair is considered beautifying or disfiguring. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, disagree on whether compensation (hukumat adl) is due for a free man. This lesson will walk you through the reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline ruling
If the beard regrows exactly as before, no compensation is due because no trace of injury remains. The perpetrator receives ta'zir for the unlawful act.
This is the default: no diyah if hair returns to original state.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position on white regrowth
For a free man, white hair increases beauty, so no compensation. For a slave, white hair reduces value, so hukumat adl is due.
Abu Hanifa distinguishes between free and slave based on market value and aesthetic perception.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that hukumat adl is due for both free and slave because white hair out of its natural time (i.e., prematurely) is disfiguring, not beautifying.
The Sahibayn do not differentiate between free and slave in this case.
4
Identify the common ground
Both sides agree that intentional and accidental acts are treated equally, and that if hair regrows normally, no diyah is due. The dispute only arises when the regrown hair is white.
The disagreement is confined to the 'white regrowth' scenario.

Source Text

If it grows white, there is a difference of opinion: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that for a free man, no diyah is due because white hair enhances beauty, whereas for a slave, hukumat adl is due because it reduces his value. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that hukumat adl is due in both cases because white hair out of season is disfiguring. In all cases, the ruling applies equally to intentional and accidental acts.

Key Terms
منبت (manbit): The growth area of the beard (root of hair).
حكومة عدل (hukumat adl): Equitable compensation determined by arbitrators based on the reduction in value.

Diyah for Paired Organs: Eyes, Hands, Feet, Lips, Ears, Testicles
Listing of paired organs with fixed diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fixed diyah amounts for paired organs and explain the underlying principle of jins al-manfa'ah.

Core Idea
Destroying both organs of a pair incurs full diyah; one organ incurs half.

This passage from Al-Quduri enumerates the paired organs for which the Shariah has prescribed a fixed diyah (blood money). The ruling is supported by hadith and by qiyas based on the loss of the entire genus of benefit (jins al-manfa'ah) or complete beauty. Understanding this list is foundational for the chapter of diyat.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the list of six pairs
Commit to memory: eyes, hands, feet, lips, ears, testicles. These are the only paired organs with fixed diyah as per the hadith.
Other pairs like eyebrows are not included; their loss is assessed by hukumat adl.
2
Note the ruling: full for pair, half for one
For each pair, destroying both incurs full diyah (100 camels or equivalent), and destroying one incurs half diyah (50 camels).
This is a fixed scale, not subject to ijtihad in amount.
3
Identify the textual proof
The passage cites two hadith sources: the hadith of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab and the letter of 'Amr ibn Hazm. Both explicitly state the full and half diyah for these organs.
The proof is ahad hadith, so the ruling is wajib, not fard.
4
Analyze the rational proof (qiyas)
The underlying principle is that the pair provides a complete genus of benefit (jins al-manfa'ah) or complete beauty. Losing both eliminates that benefit entirely, hence full diyah; losing one eliminates half, hence half diyah.
This qiyas is jaliyyah (clear analogy) based on the illa of total loss of benefit.
5
Apply the principle to each organ
For each pair, verify that the pair indeed provides a distinct benefit (e.g., sight for eyes, grasp for hands, speech and eating for lips, hearing for ears, reproduction for testicles).
The principle ensures consistency: any pair with a complete benefit would theoretically follow the same rule, but only those explicitly mentioned in the hadith are included.

Source Text

قال وفى العينين الدية وفى اليدين الدية وفى الرجلين الدية وفى الشفتين الدية وفي الاذنين الدية وفي الانثيين الدية كذا روى في حديث سعيد بن المسيب عن النبي عليه السلام قال وفي كل واحد من هذه الاشياء نصف الدية وفيما كتبه النبي عليه السلام لعمرو بن حزم وفى العينين الدية وفي احدهما نصف الدية ولان فى تفويت الاثنين من هذه الاشياء تفويت جنس المنفعة او كمال الجمال فيجب كل الدية وفى تفويت احدهما تفويت النصف فيجب نصف الدية
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور دونوں آنکھوں میں دیت ہے اور دونوں ہاتھوں میں دیت ہے اور دونوں پیروں میں دیت ہے اور دونوں ہونٹوں میں دیت ہے اور دونوں کانوں میں دیت ہے اور دونوں خصیوں میں دیت ہے، نبی علیہ السلام سے سعید بن مسیب کی حدیث میں ایسے ہی مروی ہے قدوری نے فرمایا اور ان اشیاء میں ہر ایک میں آدھی دیت ہے اور جس کتاب کو نبی علیہ السلام نے عمرو بن حزم کے لئے لکھا تھا اس میں ہے اور دونوں آنکھوں کے فوت کرنے میں جنس منفعت کو فوت کرنا ہے تو پوری دیت واجب ہوگی ، اور ان دونوں میں سے ایک کو فوت کرنے میں نصف کو فوت کرنا ہے ، تو نصف دیت واجب ہوگی۔
تشریح مطلب عبارت کا ترجمہ سے ظاہر ہے، خلاصہ کلام جہاں دونوں ہاتھ یا پیر وغیرہ کو کاٹنے سے پوری دیت واجب ہے وہاں ایک کو کاٹنے سے نصف دیت واجب ہوئی۔ سعید بن مسیب اور عمرو بن حزم کی کتاب میں اسی طرح منقول ہے اور اصول کی بات ہے کہ جب جنس منفعت یا کمال جمال کی تقویت سے پوری دیت واجب ہوئی تو نصف کی تفویت سے نصف دیت واجب ہوگی ۔
He (al-Quduri) said: For both eyes, the diyah; for both hands, the diyah; for both feet, the diyah; for both lips, the diyah; for both ears, the diyah; for both testicles, the diyah. Thus it is narrated in the hadith of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'And for each one of these things, half the diyah.' And in what the Prophet wrote to 'Amr ibn Hazm: 'For both eyes, the diyah, and for one of them, half the diyah.' And because in losing both of these things, one loses the entire genus of benefit or complete beauty, so the full diyah is obligatory. And in losing one of them, one loses half, so half the diyah is obligatory.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational list of paired organs for which fixed diyah applies. For each pair (eyes, hands, feet, lips, ears, testicles), the full diyah is due when both are destroyed, and half diyah for one. The proof comes from the hadith of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab and the letter of 'Amr ibn Hazm. The underlying principle (qiyas) is that the loss of the pair results in total loss of the benefit or beauty that the pair provides, hence full diyah; loss of one results in half, hence half diyah.

Key Terms
جنس المنفعة (jins al-manfa'ah): The entire category of benefit provided by a pair of organs (e.g., sight for eyes, grasp for hands).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Half diyah
C) Hukumat adl
D) No diyah

Key Takeaway
For each of the six paired organs listed in the hadith, destroying both incurs full diyah, and destroying one incurs half diyah.

Diyah for Woman's Breasts and Nipples, Man's Breasts
Ruling on diyah for breasts and nipples with ta'lil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah for a woman's breasts and nipples, and explain why the diyah for a man's breasts differs.

Core Idea
Woman's breasts carry full diyah because of nursing benefit; man's breasts only hukumat adl due to lack of benefit.

This passage from Al-Hidayah discusses the diyah (blood money) for destroying a person's breasts or nipples. The ruling distinguishes between a woman's breasts, which provide the benefit of nursing, and a man's breasts, which do not. Understanding the legal reasoning behind this distinction is key to applying similar cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The destruction of breasts and nipples, and the diyah owed.
There are three sub-rulings: woman's breasts, man's breasts, and woman's nipples.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is qiyas based on the illah (legal cause) of Jins al-Manfa'ah (genus of benefit) – specifically the benefit of nursing.
This is not an explicit text but an analogy drawn from the principle that organs providing a specific benefit carry full diyah.
3
Apply the ruling to a woman's breasts
Since woman's breasts provide nursing benefit, destroying both requires full diyah of the woman; destroying one requires half.
This is consistent with the general rule for paired organs that provide benefit.
4
Contrast with a man's breasts
Man's breasts do not provide nursing benefit, only beauty (jamal). Beauty alone does not warrant full diyah, so only hukumat adl (arbitrated compensation) is due.
This distinguishes man's breasts from other paired organs like eyes or hands.
5
Apply the ruling to a woman's nipples
Nipples are essential for nursing; destroying both causes full loss of benefit, so full diyah; one nipple carries half.
The same logic applies as for the breast itself.

قال وفى ثديي المرأة الدية لما فيه من تفويت جنس المنفعة وفى احدهما نصف دية المرأة لما بينا بخلاف تديى الرجل حيث تجب حكومة عدل لانه ليس فيه تفويت جنس المنفعة والجمال وفى وحلمتى المرأة الدية كاملة لفوات جنس منفعة الارضاع و امساك اللبن وفى احدهما نصفها لما بيناه.
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور عورت کے دونوں پستانوں میں پوری دیت ہے اس لئے کہ اس میں جنس منفعت کو فوت کرنا ہے اور ان میں سے ایک میں عورت کی دیت کا نصف ہے بوجہ اس کے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں بخلاف مرد کے دونوں پستانوں کے کہ یہاں حکومت عدل واجب ہے اس لئے کہ اس میں جنس منفعت اور جمال کو فوت کرنا نہیں ہے اور عورت کی پستان کے سروں میں پوری دیت ہے، منفعت ارضاع اور امساک لبن کے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے اور ان میں سے ایک میں نصف دیت ہے اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔
تشریح عورت کے دونوں پستان کاٹ دیئے گئے تو عورت کی پوری دیت واجب ہوگی، کیونکہ جنس منفعت فوت ہوگئی اور ایک کائی تو عورت کی آدھی دیت واجب ہوگی دلیل سابق کی وجہ سے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: For the two breasts of a woman, the full diyah, because it involves loss of the genus of benefit. And for one of them, half the diyah of the woman, as we have explained. Unlike the two breasts of a man, where hukumat adl is obligatory, because there is no loss of the genus of benefit and beauty. And for the two nipples of a woman, the full diyah, for the loss of the genus of benefit of nursing and retention of milk. And for one of them, half of that, as we have explained.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage explains the diyah for breasts and nipples. For a woman, both breasts carry full diyah because they provide the benefit of nursing (jins al-manfa'ah). If one breast is destroyed, half diyah of a woman (i.e., half the full diyah of a woman) is due. For a man, only hukumat adl is due because male breasts do not provide the same benefit. Similarly, both nipples of a woman carry full diyah due to the nursing benefit, and one nipple carries half diyah.

Key Terms
حلمة (halamah): Nipple of the breast.
ارضاع (irda'): Breastfeeding, the benefit provided by a woman's breasts.

D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The diyah for body parts is determined by the benefit (manfa'ah) they provide; woman's breasts and nipples carry full diyah because of nursing benefit, while man's breasts only warrant hukumat adl.

Diyah for Paired Organs: Full for Both, Half for One
States the ruling and provides proof from hadith and reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for diyah on the six specified paired organs and apply the principle of jins al-manfa'ah to determine the amount of diyah for loss of one or both organs.

Core Idea
For any paired organ: full diyah for both, half diyah for one.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on diyah for paired organs. The source passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a clear principle: when both organs of a pair (eyes, hands, feet, lips, ears, testicles) are destroyed, full diyah is due; when only one is destroyed, half diyah is due. The ruling is supported by prophetic reports and a rational principle tying diyah to the loss of the genus of benefit (jins al-manfa'ah) or perfect beauty (kamal al-jamal).

Guided Path
1
List the paired organs
Identify the six pairs mentioned: eyes, hands, feet, lips, ears, testicles.
These are the organs specified in the hadith and the matn.
2
State the ruling for each pair
For each pair, the ruling is: full diyah for both, half diyah for one.
3
Examine the dalil
The passage cites two hadith sources: the hadith of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib and the letter of Amr ibn Hazm, both explicitly stating half diyah for a single organ and full diyah for the pair.
These are ahad hadith, but their meaning (dalala) is clear (qati).
4
Understand the rational principle
The underlying principle is that destroying both organs eliminates the entire genus of benefit (e.g., sight for eyes) or perfect beauty, thus full diyah. Destroying one eliminates half, so half diyah is due.
This principle confirms the hadith ruling and can be applied analogically.

قال وفى العينين الدية وفى اليدين الدية وفى الرجلين الدية وفى الشفتين الدية وفي الاذنين الدية وفي الانثيين الدية كذا روى في حديث سعيد بن المسيب عن النبي عليه السلام قال وفي كل واحد من هذه الاشياء نصف الدية وفيما كتبه النبي عليه السلام لعمرو بن حزم وفى العينين الدية وفي احدهما نصف الدية ولان فى تفويت الاثنين من هذه الاشياء تفويت جنس المنفعة او كمال الجمال فيجب كل الدية وفى تفويت احدهما تفويت النصف فيجب نصف الدية

Book of Blood Money. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 15. Which cutting of limbs gives full diyah and which gives half diyah. He said: In the two eyes is full diyah, in the two hands is full diyah, in the two feet is full diyah, in the two lips is full diyah, in the two ears is full diyah, in the two testicles is full diyah. Thus it is narrated in the hadith of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib from the Prophet (peace be upon him): And in each one of these things is half the diyah. And in what the Prophet (peace be upon him) wrote to Amr ibn Hazm: In the two eyes is full diyah, and in one of them is half the diyah. And because in destroying both of these things there is destruction of the genus of benefit or of perfect beauty, so full diyah is obligatory, and in destroying one of them there is destruction of half, so half diyah is obligatory. Translation: Quduri said: In both eyes is diyah, in both hands is diyah, in both feet is diyah, in both lips is diyah, in both ears is diyah, in both testicles is diyah. It is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Sa'id ibn Musayyib similarly. Quduri said: And in each of these things is half the diyah. And in the book that the Prophet (peace be upon him) wrote to Amr ibn Hazm: In destroying both eyes, there is destruction of the genus of benefit, so full diyah becomes obligatory, and in destroying one of them, there is destruction of half, so half diyah becomes obligatory. Commentary: The meaning of the phrase is clear from the translation. Summary: Where cutting both hands or feet etc. gives full diyah, cutting one gives half diyah. It is narrated in the book of Sa'id ibn Musayyib and Amr ibn Hazm similarly. And it is a matter of principle: when full diyah is obligatory due to loss of genus of benefit or perfect beauty, then loss of half gives half diyah.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil). The author, Imam Quduri, states that for paired organs — eyes, hands, feet, lips, ears, testicles — cutting off both requires full diyah (blood money), and cutting off one requires half diyah. The proof is from two sources: first, the hadith of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib from the Prophet (peace be upon him) which explicitly states half diyah for each of these single organs; second, the letter written by the Prophet to Amr ibn Hazm which mentions full diyah for both eyes and half for one. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that destroying both destroys the entire genus of benefit (jins al-manfa'ah) of that organ pair or perfect beauty (kamal al-jamal), so full diyah is due. Destroying one destroys half of that, so half diyah is due. The commentary explains that this principle applies to all such paired organs. In the Hanafi school, this ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is relied upon (mufta bihi). The diyah for these major limbs is fixed, not subject to ijtihad.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money; financial compensation paid for bodily injury or homicide, as prescribed by shariah.
جنس المنفعة (jins al-manfa'ah): The genus or category of benefit; here, the essential benefit provided by a paired organ (e.g., sight for eyes, grip for hands).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the diyah for cutting off one eye?
A) Full diyah
B) Half diyah
C) One-fourth diyah
D) No diyah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that for any of the six specified paired organs, destruction of both requires full diyah, and destruction of one requires half diyah, based on prophetic reports and the principle of loss of the genus of benefit.

Diyah for Breasts and Nipples: Woman vs Man
Ruling on diyah for breasts and nipples with ta'lil (reasoning).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for diyah on a woman's breasts/nipples and a man's breasts, and explain the reasoning based on jins al-manfa'ah and jamal.

Core Idea
A woman's breasts trigger full diyah for benefit; a man's breasts only hukumat al-adl as no such benefit is lost.

This lesson details the Hanafi position on diyah for injuries to the breasts and nipples. The key distinction is between a woman's breasts, which serve the genus of benefit (jins al-manfa'ah) of breastfeeding and contribute to beauty, and a man's breasts, which lack these functions. The ruling is derived from the general principle that fixed diyah applies where a complete genus of benefit is lost, otherwise discretionary compensation (hukumat al-adl) is assessed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the injuries covered
The passage addresses four cases: both breasts of a woman, one breast, both nipples (halamah), and both breasts of a man. For each, determine the compensation type.
2
State the ruling for each case
For a woman: full diyah for both breasts/nipples, half for one. For a man: hukumat al-adl for both breasts. Note that a woman's diyah is half of a man's, so 'half the woman's diyah' is one-quarter of a man's diyah in absolute terms.
3
Locate the proof (ta'lil)
The reasoning is based on the presence or absence of jins al-manfa'ah (genus of benefit) and kamal al-jamal (perfect beauty). For a woman, cutting both breasts destroys the benefit of breastfeeding and beauty, hence full diyah. For a man, no such loss, so only hukumat al-adl.
4
Understand the distinction for nipples
Nipples are essential for breastfeeding and milk retention. Therefore, they are treated like breasts: full diyah for both, half for one. The same reasoning applies.
5
Apply the rule to similar cases
Consider other body parts where benefit is gender-specific. For example, a woman's ability to bear children may affect diyah for certain organs. The Hanafi school consistently uses jins al-manfa'ah as a criterion.

قال وفى ثديي المرأة الدية لما فيه من تفويت جنس المنفعة وفى احدهما نصف دية المرأة لما بينا بخلاف تديى الرجل حيث تجب حكومة عدل لانه ليس فيه تفويت جنس المنفعة والجمال وفى وحلمتى المرأة الدية كاملة لفوات جنس منفعة الارضاع و امساك اللبن وفى احدهما نصفها لما بيناه. ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور عورت کے دونوں پستانوں میں پوری دیت ہے اس لئے کہ اس میں جنس منفعت کو فوت کرنا ہے اور ان میں سے ایک میں عورت کی دیت کا نصف ہے بوجہ اس کے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں بخلاف مرد کے دونوں پستانوں کے کہ یہاں حکومت عدل واجب ہے اس لئے کہ اس میں جنس منفعت اور جمال کو فوت کرنا نہیں ہے اور عورت کی پستان کے سروں میں پوری دیت ہے، منفعت ارضاع اور امساک لبن کے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے اور ان میں سے ایک میں نصف دیت ہے اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح عورت کے دونوں پستان کاٹ دیئے گئے تو عورت کی پوری دیت واجب ہوگی، کیونکہ جنس منفعت فوت ہوگئی اور ایک کائی تو عورت کی آدھی دیت واجب ہوگی دلیل سابق کی وجہ سے۔

كتاب الديات
اور اگر مرد کی دونوں پستان کاٹ دیئے گئے تو اس میں صرف حکومت عدل واجب ہے کیونکہ اس میں نہ جنس منفعت کی تقویت ہے اور نہ جمال کی ، کما ہو ظا ہر ہا۔
اور اگر عورت کی پستان کا سرا ( ٹونڈنا) کاٹا گیا تو دونوں کی صورت میں عورت کی پوری دیت اور ایک کی صورت میں آدھی دیت واجب ہوگی۔
کیونکہ ٹونڈنے کے بغیر دودھ پلایا جا سکتا ہے اور نہ دودھ پستان میں رک سکتا ہے۔
In cutting off both breasts of a woman is full diyah, and in one is half diyah; and in cutting off both breasts of a man, government of 'adl is obligatory. He said: In the two breasts of a woman is full diyah because there is destruction of the genus of benefit, and in one of them is half the diyah of the woman as we have explained, unlike the breasts of a man where government of 'adl is obligatory because there is no destruction of the genus of benefit or beauty. And in the two nipples of a woman is full diyah due to loss of the genus of the benefit of breastfeeding and retention of milk, and in one of them is half as we have explained. Translation: Quduri said: In both breasts of a woman is full diyah because there is destruction of genus of benefit, and in one of them is half of the woman's diyah as we have explained, unlike the breasts of a man where government of 'adl is obligatory because there is no destruction of genus of benefit or beauty. And in the nipples of a woman is full diyah due to loss of the benefit of breastfeeding and retention of milk, and in one of them is half due to the same proof that we have explained. Commentary: If both breasts of a woman are cut off, her full diyah becomes obligatory because the genus of benefit is lost; if one is cut, half her diyah becomes obligatory due to the previous proof. And if the breasts of a man are cut off, only government of 'adl is obligatory because there is neither loss of genus of benefit nor beauty, as is apparent. And if the tip (nipple) of a woman's breast is cut off, in the case of both, the woman's full diyah and in the case of one, half diyah becomes obligatory, because without the nipple neither can milk be fed nor can milk be retained in the breast.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage provides rulings for breasts and nipples with clear distinction between woman and man. For a woman, both breasts provide the benefit of breastfeeding and contribute to beauty; cutting both destroys the genus of benefit, so full diyah (the woman's full diyah, which is half of a man's diyah) is due. Cutting one destroys half, so half of her diyah is due. The same rule applies to her nipples (halamah) because they are essential for breastfeeding and milk retention. For a man, breasts have no such benefit and do not significantly affect beauty, so cutting them only requires 'hukumat al-adl' (government of 'adl) — a discretionary compensation assessed by a judge, not a fixed diyah. The reasoning (ta'lil) is based on the presence or absence of jins al-manfa'ah and kamal al-jamal. This is a well-established Hanafi position from the zahir al-riwayah. Note that the woman's diyah is half of a man's, so 'half the woman's diyah' means one-quarter of a man's diyah in absolute terms.

Key Terms
حكومة عدل (hukumat al-adl): A discretionary financial compensation assessed by a judge when there is no fixed diyah; based on the decrease in value of the person due to the injury.
حلمة (halamah): Nipple of the breast; its removal is considered separately in diyah due to its crucial role in breastfeeding.
جنس المنفعة (jins al-manfa'ah): Genus of benefit; a category of functional utility that, if entirely lost, triggers a fixed diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Full diyah of a woman
B) Half diyah of a woman
C) Hukumat al-adl
D) One-fourth diyah

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, fixed diyah for breasts applies only when the injury destroys a complete genus of benefit, as in a woman's breasts; for a man, only discretionary compensation is due.

Diyah for Eyelashes: Proportional Calculation and Terminological Clarification
Ruling on diyah for eyelashes/eyelids with terminological discussion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah amounts for cutting one, three, and four eyelashes and explain the Hanafi reasoning based on loss of beauty and protection benefit.

Core Idea
Cutting all four eyelashes incurs full diyah; cutting one gives quarter diyah — beauty and eye protection are proportionally lost.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on diyah for eyelashes. It covers the terminological ambiguity of the term 'ashfar' and the proportional calculation of diyah based on the number of eyelashes. You will learn how the jurists derived the amounts from the principle of compensating lost benefit and beauty.

Guided Path
1
Clarify the terminology
Understand that 'ashfar' can mean the edge of the eyelid or be used metaphorically for the eyelashes themselves. The ruling applies to both interpretations, so the exact referent does not change the outcome.
The metaphor is based on adjacency (mujawarah), similar to using 'rawiyah' (camel) for the waterskin it carries.
2
Identify the total number
Note that there are four eyelashes in total (upper and lower for each eye). This is the basis for the proportional calculation.
3
Apply the proportionality principle
Full diyah is due for all four. Since the loss of benefit and beauty is complete when all are cut, each eyelash represents one-quarter of the total. Thus, one eyelash gives quarter diyah; three give three-quarters diyah.
This is a simple fractional deduction from the full diyah.
4
Understand the rationale
The diyah compensates for two things: loss of perfect beauty and loss of the genus of benefit (protection from dust and debris). Cutting all four eliminates both completely; cutting fewer reduces the loss proportionally.
The benefit is specifically the removal of annoyance (adha) and debris (qadha) from the eye.
5
Consider the proof structure
The ruling is derived from the nature of the body part and the general principle that diyah for parts that cannot be measured precisely is based on estimated harm. Here, the harm is quantifiable by counting the units (eyelashes).
This is talil (causal reasoning) rather than direct textual proof.

آنکھوں کی پلکوں میں پوری دیت اور ایک میں ربع دیت ہے۔
قال وفى اشفار العينين الدية وفى احدها ربع الدية قال رضى الله عنه يحتمل ان مراده الاهداب مجازا كما ذكر محمد في الاصل للمجاورة كالرواية لقربة وهي حقيقة في البعير وهذا لانه يفوت به الجمال على الكمال وجنس المنفعة وهى منفعة دفع الاذى والقذى عن العين اذهو يندفع بالهدب واذا كان الواجب في الكل كل الداية وهى اربعة كان فى احدهما ربع الدية وفى ثلثة منها ثلثة ارباعها ويحتمل ان يكون مراده منبت الشعر والحكم فيه هكذا
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور آنکھوں کی پلکوں میں پوری دیت ہے اور ان میں سے ایک میں چوتھائی دیت ہے مصنف نے فرمایا احتمال ہے کہ اشفار سے مراد اہداب ( پلیس ) ہوں مجاز ا جیسا کہ محمد نے مبسوط میں ذکر کیا ہے مجاورت کی وجہ سے جیسے راو یہ مشکیزہ کے لئے اور راد یہ اونٹ میں حقیقت ہے اور یہ اس لئے کہ اس سے کامل جمال فوت ہو جاتا ہے اور جنس منفعت فوت ہو جاتی ہے اور منفعت تکلیف اور خس وخاشاک کو دور کرنے کی منفعت ہے آنکھ سے اور اس لئے کہ یہ ( اذگی اور قذی ) پلکوں سے دور ہوتی ہے اور جب تمام پلکوں میں پوری دیت واجب ہے اور پلکیں چار ہیں تو ان میں سے ایک میں چوتھائی دیت ہوگی اور ان میں سے تین میں تین چوتھائی اور احتمال ہے کہ مصنف کی مراد منبت الشعر ہوا دار اس میں بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ تشریح اشفار کے معنی ہیں پلک کی جڑ یعنی جہاں پلکیں اگتی ہیں وہ جگہ اور اہداب کے معنی ہیں پلکیں لیکن ان دونوں میں مجاورت کا تعلق ہے جو مجاز مرسل کا علاقہ ہے لہذا ایک کو دوسرے کے معنی میں استعمال کر لیا جاتا ہے جیسے راویہ کے معنی اونٹ اور اس کے اوپر پانی کا مشکیزہ ( پکھال ) رکھ کر لاتے ہیں تو اونٹ اور پکھال میں مجاورت کا تعلق ہے تو راویہ مجاز مشکیزہ ( پکھال کو کہدیتے ہیں۔ لہذا قد دوری کے متن میں لفظ اشفار سے پلکیں بھی مراد ہو سکتی ہیں اور پیک کی جز بھی بہر حال حکم دونوں کا ایک ہے۔ پلکیں کل چار ہوتی ہیں اور ان کی جڑیں بھی چار ہوتی ہیں۔ تو اگر کسی نے پوری پلکیں کاٹ دیں تو پوری دیت واجب ہوگی اور اگر ایک کائی تو چونکہ ایک کل کا ۱۴ ہے تو دیت نام ہی واجب ہو گی۔وقس على هذا بہر حال تمام پلکوں کے کاٹنے سے پوری دیت اس لئے واجب ہوگی کہ جنس منفعت بھی فوت ہوگئی اور جمال بھی فوت ہو گیا ، پلکوں کی منفعت یہ ہے کہ ان کے ذریعہ تکلیف دہ چیز مثلا گردو غبار اور خس و خاشاک آنکھ میں نہیں پہنچ پاتے ۔
In the eyelashes of the two eyes is full diyah, and in one of them is quarter diyah. He said: In the ashfar (eyelids/eyelashes) of the two eyes is full diyah, and in one of them is quarter diyah. The author (may Allah be pleased with him) said: It is possible that he means by ashfar the ahdab (eyelashes) metaphorically, as Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl, due to adjacency, like 'rawiyah' for waterskin, while it is literally a camel. And this is because it causes loss of perfect beauty and the genus of benefit, which is the benefit of removing annoyance and dust from the eye, as it is removed by the eyelashes. And when the obligatory for all is full diyah, and they are four, then in one is quarter diyah, and in three is three-quarters. And it is possible that he means the root of the hair, and the ruling is the same. Translation: Quduri said: In the eyelashes of the eyes is full diyah, and in one of them is quarter diyah. The author said: It is possible that by ashfar he means ahdab (eyelashes) metaphorically, as Muhammad mentioned in al-Mabsut due to adjacency, like 'rawiyah' for waterskin while it is literally a camel. And this is because it causes loss of perfect beauty and the genus of benefit, which is the benefit of removing annoyance and dust from the eye, as it is removed by the eyelashes. And when full diyah is obligatory for all, and they are four, then in one is quarter diyah, and in three is three-quarters. And it is possible that he means the hair root, and the ruling is the same. Commentary: Ashfar means the root of the eyelid, i.e., the place where eyelashes grow, and ahdab means the eyelashes themselves. But there is a relationship of adjacency between them, which is the basis of majaz mursal, so one can be used in the meaning of the other. For example, 'rawiyah' is used for the camel that carries a waterskin, and also metaphorically for the waterskin itself. So in Quduri's text, the word ashfar can mean both the eyelids and the eyelashes; in either case, the ruling is the same. Eyelashes are four in total, and their roots are also four. So if someone cuts all eyelashes, full diyah is obligatory, and if one, then since one is one-fourth of the total, quarter diyah is obligatory. Qiyas on this. In any case, cutting all eyelashes gives full diyah because both the genus of benefit and beauty are lost. The benefit of eyelashes is to prevent harmful things like dust and debris from reaching the eye.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling for the eyelashes or eyelids (ashfar/ahdab). The matn of Quduri states that for the ashfar of both eyes, full diyah is due; for one, quarter diyah. The commentator mentions a terminological possibility: 'ashfar' may be used metaphorically to mean the eyelashes themselves (ahdab) due to adjacency (mujawarah), as explained by Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut. The example given is 'rawiyah', which literally means a camel but can refer to the waterskin it carries. Regardless of the exact meaning, the ruling is the same because the loss of benefit (preventing dust and harm) and beauty applies to both. Since the eyelashes are four (upper and lower for each eye), cutting all four causes loss of complete genus of benefit and perfect beauty, so full diyah is due. Cutting one means losing one-fourth, so quarter diyah is due. Cutting three gives three-quarters. This reasoning is based on proportionality. The Hanafi position is that these fixed diyah amounts are from zahir al-riwayah and are mufta bihi.

Key Terms
اشفار (ashfar): Usually means the edges of the eyelids where eyelashes grow; here used metaphorically to refer to the eyelashes themselves.
اهداب (ahdab): The eyelashes themselves; the literal meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the diyah for cutting three eyelashes?
A) Full diyah
B) Three-quarters diyah
C) Half diyah
D) Quarter diyah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi diyah for eyelashes is proportional to the number of eyelashes cut: full for all four, quarter for one, three-quarters for three, based on loss of beauty and protective benefit.

Diyah for Cutting Male and Female Breasts
Explaining diyah for male breasts and female nipples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah rulings for cutting male breasts and female nipples, and explain the underlying legal reason (illa) based on independent benefit and beauty.

Core Idea
Diyah is for a part with independent benefit or beauty; male breasts lack both, so hukumat adl; female nipples have benefit, so full diyah.

In this lesson, we examine a short but important passage from the Hanafi fiqh on diyat. The text distinguishes between male and female breasts, and between cutting both nipples versus one. The compensation hinges on whether the lost part has an independent function and beauty. Understanding this principle helps in applying diyah rules to other body parts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage deals with two distinct cases: cutting both breasts of a man, and cutting the nipple(s) of a woman. Separate them in your mind.
2
State the ruling for each
For a man: both breasts cut → hukumat adl (equitable compensation). For a woman: both nipples cut → full diyah; one nipple cut → half diyah.
Note: 'full diyah' here means the diyah of a woman, which is half that of a man according to Hanafi.
3
Extract the legal reason (illa)
Identify why each ruling is given. The text states: for male breasts, no strengthening of benefit (manfa'ah) nor beauty (jamal); for female nipple, essential for breastfeeding.
The word 'because' (کیونکہ) indicates the illa.
4
Connect to the general principle
The Hanafi school holds that full diyah is due for a body part that has an independent benefit or contributes to beauty. If a part lacks both, only hukumat adl applies.
This principle is not stated in the passage but is the underlying rule.
5
Apply to other parts
Think of other body parts: ears (benefit of hearing), nose (smell, beauty), etc. Would they get diyah? This exercise strengthens your understanding.
This step goes beyond the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اگر مرد کی دونوں پستان کاٹ دیئے گئے تو اس میں صرف حکومت عدل واجب ہے کیونکہ اس میں نہ جنس منفعت کی تقویت ہے اور نہ جمال کی ، کما ہو ظا ہر ہا۔ اور اگر عورت کی پستان کا سرا ( ٹونڈنا) کاٹا گیا تو دونوں کی صورت میں عورت کی پوری دیت اور ایک کی صورت میں آدھی دیت واجب ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ٹونڈنے کے بغیر دودھ پلایا جا سکتا ہے اور نہ دودھ پستان میں رک سکتا ہے۔
And if both breasts of a man are cut off, then in that only hukumat adl (equitable compensation) is obligatory, because in it there is neither strengthening of the species of benefit nor of beauty, as is apparent. And if the tip (nipple) of a woman's breast is cut, then in the case of both, the full diyah of the woman is obligatory, and in the case of one, half the diyah is obligatory, because without the nipple, milk cannot be suckled and milk cannot remain in the breast.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on diyah for cutting breasts. For a man, cutting both breasts only requires hukumat adl (an equitable assessment by the judge, not a fixed diyah) because breasts in men have neither the function of milk production (manfa'ah) nor significant beauty (jamal). For a woman, the nipple (sarā/ṭonḍnā) is essential for breastfeeding. Therefore, cutting both nipples results in full diyah, and cutting one results in half diyah, as the loss of the ability to nurse is a major loss of benefit. This ruling is based on the Hanafi principle that diyah is due only when a complete member with an independent benefit is lost.

Key Terms
حکومت عدل (ḥukūmat ʿadl): Compensation assessed by a fair judge when no fixed diyah is prescribed.
دیت (diyah): Monetary compensation payable for homicide or bodily harm, specified by shari'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a woman's single nipple is cut off?
A) Hukumat adl
B) Half of the full diyah
C) Full diyah
D) No compensation

Key Takeaway
The compensation for a lost body part depends on its independent benefit and beauty; male breasts have neither, so hukumat adl; female nipples have benefit, so full/half diyah.

Diyah for Eyelashes (Ashfar)
Explaining diyah for eyelashes with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah for cutting eyelashes and explain the reasoning based on loss of beauty and benefit.

Core Idea
Full diyah for all eyelashes; quarter per set due to complete loss of beauty and benefit.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar addresses the diyah (blood money) for cutting the eyelashes (ashfar). The Hanafi school holds that full diyah is due for all four sets (upper and lower of both eyes), and a quarter for each set. The reasoning ties to the complete loss of both aesthetic and protective functions of the lashes. The commentary clarifies the term 'ashfar' can refer to the lashes themselves figuratively.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly triggers the diyah? Cutting the eyelashes. The ruling is that diyah is wajib (obligatory) if the loss is complete.
2
Examine the division into sets
How many sets of eyelashes are there? The text assumes four: upper and lower for each eye. The full diyah is divided equally among them.
Each set is considered an independent unit.
3
Understand the textual interpretation
The term 'ashfar' can mean the roots (literal) or the lashes themselves (figuratively). The commentator explains that both yield the same ruling because the loss is identical.
This is majaz mursal based on contiguity.
4
Trace the rationale (illa)
Why is full diyah due? Because the lashes provide both beauty (jamal) and a benefit (manfa'ah) of repelling dirt and harm. Complete loss of both constitutes a complete loss of a non-bone, non-major-organ body part with independent benefit.
This is the basis for the ruling in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Apply the ruling to partial loss
If only one set is lost, quarter diyah. For three sets, three-quarters. The division is proportional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آنکھوں کی پلکوں میں پوری دیت اور ایک میں ربع دیت ہے۔ قال وفى اشفار العينين الدية وفى احدها ربع الدية قال رضى الله عنه يحتمل ان مراده الاهداب مجازا كما ذكر محمد في الاصل للمجاورة كالرواية لقربة وهي حقيقة في البعير وهذا لانه يفوت به الجمال على الكمال وجنس المنفعة وهى منفعة دفع الاذى والقذى عن العين اذهو يندفع بالهدب واذا كان الواجب في الكل كل الداية وهى اربعة كان فى احدهما ربع الدية وفى ثلثة منها ثلثة ارباعها ويحتمل ان يكون مراده منبت الشعر والحكم فيه هكذا
In the eyelashes of the eyes is the full diyah, and in one of them is a quarter of the diyah. He (al-Quduri) said: And in the ashfar (roots/fringes) of the two eyes is the full diyah, and in one of them is a quarter of the diyah. The author (radiya Allahu 'anhu) said: It is possible that his intention is the lashes (ahdab) figuratively, as Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl, due to contiguity (mujawarah), like al-rawiyah for the waterskin, while it is literally for the camel. And this is because by it (cutting) beauty is lost completely, and the genus of benefit (manfa'ah) is lost, and it is the benefit of repelling harm and dust from the eye, because they (harm/dust) are repelled by the lashes. And when the obligation for the whole is the full diyah, and they are four, so in one of them is a quarter of the diyah, and in three of them is three-quarters. And it is possible that his intention is the place where the hair grows (manbat al-sha'r), and the ruling is likewise.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the diyah for the ashfar (eyelashes or their roots). The matn of al-Quduri states that full diyah is due for both eyes' ashfar and quarter diyah for one. The commentator explains two interpretations of 'ashfar': (1) the lashes themselves (ahdab) by way of metonymy (majaz mursal) due to contiguity; (2) the hair-growing area (manbat al-sha'r). In either case, the ruling is the same. The reasoning is that lashes provide both beauty (jamal) and a benefit (manfa'ah)—repelling dirt and harmful particles from the eye. Since there are four sets of lashes (upper and lower for each eye), full diyah is divided equally: quarter per set. This ruling is from the Hanafi school, based on the principle of loss of independent benefit and beauty.

Key Terms
أشفار (ashfār): Eyelash roots or the lashes themselves; here used metonymically for lashes.
أهداب (ahdāb): The eyelashes (the hairs themselves).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the diyah for cutting one of the four sets of eyelashes?
A) Full diyah
B) Half diyah
C) Quarter diyah
D) One-tenth diyah

Key Takeaway
Full diyah is wajib for loss of all eyelashes, divided equally among the four sets, because of the complete loss of beauty and protective benefit.

One Diyah for the Eyelid Unit
One full diyah for cutting eyelids and lashes together

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that composite members constitute a single unit for diyah, and analogize using the nose as the original case.

Core Idea
Eyelids and lashes form one unit – one diyah, not two.

This passage answers whether cutting both eyelids and eyelashes in one act incurs one or two diyahs. The Hanafi school rules one diyah because they function as a single cosmetic and protective unit. The ruling is justified by qiyas on the nose, where cutting cartilage (marin) and bone (qasabah) together also gives one diyah.

Guided Path
1
State the case and ruling
Identify the act: cutting the eyelids (جفون) with their lashes (أهداب). The ruling: one diyah is wajib.
The text says 'ففيه دية واحدة' – one diyah in it.
2
Identify the effective cause (illa)
The text gives the illa: 'لان الكل كشئ واحد' – because the whole is like a single thing. Both parts together form one functional and aesthetic unit.
The illa is the unity of the member, not the number of parts cut.
3
Recognize the qiyas
The ruling is analogized to the nose: just as cutting cartilage (مارن) with bone (قصبة) yields one diyah, so does cutting eyelids with lashes. The common illa is that each pair forms a single composite member.
This is qiyas jaliy – the analogy is clear and explicit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پلکیں اور جڑیں کاٹ دیں تو ایک دیت واجب ہے ولو قطع الجفون باهدا بها ففيه دية واحدة لان الكل كشئ واحد وصار كالمارن مع القصبة
If one cuts the eyelids along with the roots (lashes), then one diyah is obligatory. And if one cuts the eyelids with their lashes, then in it is one diyah, because the whole is like a single thing, and it becomes like the cartilage of the nose (marin) with the nasal bone (qasabah).
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for cutting both the eyelids (jufun) and the eyelashes (ahdab) in a single act. The matn states that only one diyah is due, because the eyelids and lashes together are considered a single member (the eyelid unit) in terms of compensation. This is analogous to the nose: if one cuts the cartilage (marin) along with the nasal bone (qasabah), only one diyah is due, not separate compensations for each part. The Hanafi school thus does not double-count when multiple parts of a single functional unit are injured simultaneously. The ruling applies whether one cuts both eyelids and lashes of both eyes (full diyah) or just one set (half diyah? The text does not elaborate, but by analogy, if only one eyelid and its lashes are cut, half diyah would likely apply).

Key Terms
جفون (jufūn): Eyelids covering the eye.
مارن (mārin): The soft cartilage of the nose (nose tip).
قصبة (qaṣabah): The nasal bone (bridge).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone cuts both eyelids and all lashes of both eyes in one act, what diyah is due?
A) Two diyahs (one for eyelids, one for lashes)
B) One full diyah
C) Half diyah
D) Four diyahs

Key Takeaway
When cutting a composite member like eyelids with lashes, only one diyah is due because they form a single functional and cosmetic unit.

Rulings on Fingers: Each Finger 1/10, All Equal
Explaining the diyah for fingers of hands and feet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for diyah on fingers and toes and explain the evidence from hadith and qiyas that supports it.

Core Idea
Each finger or toe carries 1/10 of full diyah; all fingers equal, regardless of size or function.

In the Hanafi school, the diyah for cutting a finger is fixed at one-tenth (1/10) of the full diyah, based on the Prophetic hadith 'In every finger is ten camels' and a qiyas argument of equal essential benefit. This lesson will guide you through the proof structure and the principle that all fingers—whether thumb, index, or toe—carry the same compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled? The amputation (cutting off) of one finger of the hand or toe of the foot. The ruling is that wajib compensation is 1/10 of the full diyah (i.e., 10 camels out of 100).
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith directly quoted: 'في كل اصبع عشر من الابل' (In every finger is ten camels). This is a hadith ahad, so its thubut is zanni, but its dalala is clear in setting a fixed amount.
The hadith is general, covering all fingers without distinction.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith states ten camels per finger. Since the full diyah is 100 camels, each finger equals one-tenth. This is a straightforward numerical deduction.
Full diyah is established as 100 camels by other texts and ijma.
4
Analyze the qiyas supporting argument
The passage also argues via qiyas: cutting all ten fingers destroys the genus of benefit (manfa'ah asliyyah) of the hand, which warrants full diyah. Since there are ten fingers, each finger's share is one-tenth by division.
The same reasoning applies to toes, as cutting all ten toes destroys the benefit of walking.
5
Recognize the consequence: equality of all fingers
All fingers (thumb, index, etc.) and all toes are equal in diyah. The hadith's generality and the qiyas on equal original benefit prevent considering differences in size or function.
This is explicitly stated: 'والاصابع كلها سواء' (all fingers are equal).

In the fingers of both hands and both feet is the full diyah. He (al-Quduri) said: And in every finger of the fingers of the hands and feet is one-tenth of the diyah, due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'In every finger is ten camels,' and because in cutting all of them is the loss (tafwit) of the genus of benefit, and in it is a complete diyah, and they are ten, so the diyah is divided upon them. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And in every finger of the fingers of both hands and both feet is one-tenth of the diyah, due to the command of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that in every finger is ten camels, and because in cutting all the fingers is the loss (taqwiyat? read tafwit) of the genus of benefit, and in that (loss of genus of benefit) is full diyah. And the fingers are ten, so the diyah is divided upon them. Explanation: In one hand are five fingers, in two hands ten, and similarly in both feet ten, and in both hands or their ten fingers the full diyah is obligatory, and each finger is one-tenth of all the fingers of the hands, so in each finger one-tenth (1/10) of the full diyah is obligatory. The rest is clear. All fingers of the hands and all fingers of the feet are equal. He (al-Quduri) said: And all fingers are equal due to the generality of the hadith, and because they are equal in the original benefit, so increase (in size) is not considered, like the right (hand) with the left. And likewise the fingers of the feet, because by cutting all of them the benefit of walking is lost, so the full diyah is obligatory. Then in both (hands and feet) are ten fingers, so the diyah is divided upon them into tenths.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage covers the diyah for fingers. The matn of al-Quduri states: each finger (of hands and feet) carries one-tenth (1/10) of the full diyah. The proof is a hadith (attributed to the Prophet, peace be upon him) that each finger has a diyah of ten camels (since full diyah is 100 camels, each finger is 10 camels = 1/10). In the Hanafi school, all fingers—whether of hand or foot, whether thumb or pinky, right or left—are equal in diyah. This is because the original benefit (manfa'ah asliyyah) is the same: grasping for hands, walking for feet. Differences in size or specific function do not affect compensation. The same principle applies to toes: cutting all ten toes results in full diyah. The text emphasizes that the diyah is divided equally among the ten fingers of each hand and foot (though note: hands and feet together would be 20? Actually the text says hands and feet each have ten fingers? No, hands have ten fingers total (five each), feet have ten toes total. But the passage seems to consider fingers (اصابع) of hands and feet separately. For hands, cutting all ten fingers gives full diyah. For feet, cutting all ten toes gives full diyah. And each finger/toe is 1/10 of that full diyah. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
إصبع (iṣbaʿ): A finger of the hand or toe of the foot.
عشر الدية (ʿushr al-diyah): One-tenth of the full diyah.

One Diyah for Cutting Eyelids with Roots
Ruling on diyah for cutting eyelids with roots

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on diyah for cutting eyelids with roots and explain the qiyas with the nose.

Core Idea
Cutting eyelids with their roots incurs one diyah because they form a single functional unit.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses a specific injury: cutting the eyelids along with the roots of the eyelashes. The ruling is that a single complete diyah is due, analogized to cutting the nose with its cartilage. Understanding this rule requires appreciating how the Hanafi fiqh treats composite parts as a single organ for diyah purposes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is cutting the eyelids (jufun) with their roots (ahdab). Note: ahdab refers to the area where eyelashes grow, not just the hairs.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is wajib: one full diyah is due for this act.
The diyah is a fixed compensation for bodily harm.
3
Understand the reasoning (illah)
The reason given is that 'all is like one thing' (al-kull ka-shay' wahid). The eyelids and roots are treated as an integral unit.
4
Recognize the analogy (qiyas)
The ruling is analogized to cutting the nose (marin) with its cartilage (qasaba), which also incurs one full diyah. The illah is that both are single functional units.
This is qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
5
Apply the principle
If an injury involves parts that are integral to a single organ, only one diyah is due. If parts are separate, multiple diyahs may apply.
This principle prevents overcompensation for connected parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قطع الجفون بأهدابها ففيه دية واحدة لان الكل كشئ واحد وصار كالمارن مع القصبة ترجمہ اور اگر پلکوں کو مع جڑوں کے کاٹ دیا تو اس میں ایک دیت واجب ہوگی اس لئے کہ کل شئی واحد کے مثل ہے اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے فیشوم کے ساتھ نرمہ بینی ۔ تشریح یہاں اہداب سے منبت الشعر مراد ہے اور مطلب یہ ہے کہ پلکیں اور جڑیں دونوں جیسے نرمہ بینی اور بانسہ کاٹنے میں ایک ہی دیت واجب ہوتی ہے (کمامر ---
And if he cuts the eyelids with their lashes, then in that is one diyah, because all is like one thing, and it becomes like the nose with the cartilage.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from Al-Quduri on the diyah for cutting the eyelids along with their roots (the area where the eyelashes grow). The ruling is that a single complete diyah is due, because the eyelids and their roots are considered a single organ, analogous to the nose including its cartilage. In Hanafi fiqh, cutting the nose alone incurs full diyah, and similarly, cutting the eyelids with their roots is treated as one integral part. The Urdu commentary clarifies that 'ahdab' here means the place where the hair grows, i.e., the roots. Therefore, cutting both the eyelids and their roots together does not result in multiple diyahs but only one.

Key Terms

أهداب (ahdab): the roots of the eyelashes (the place where they grow)
دية (diyah): blood money; financial compensation for bodily harm or homicide

Key Takeaway
Cutting eyelids with their roots incurs one full diyah because they are treated as a single organ analogous to the nose.
