The Diyah for Each Finger of the Hands and Feet
Ruling on diyah for each finger

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah for each finger according to the Hanafi school and explain the proof from hadith and the reasoning of benefit.

Core Idea
Each finger, whether of hand or foot, incurs one-tenth of full diyah.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a clear ruling: every finger of the hands and feet carries a fixed compensation of one-tenth of the full diyah. The ruling is grounded in a prophetic hadith and a rational argument about the loss of benefit. Understanding this helps us see how Hanafi jurisprudence consistently applies textual evidence and legal reasoning to bodily injury compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is cutting (or causing loss of) a finger. The ruling is that the perpetrator must pay one-tenth of the full diyah (10 camels) for each finger.
Full diyah is 100 camels or equivalent.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the prophetic hadith: 'In every finger, ten camels.' This is a direct textual evidence (dalil naqli).
The hadith is ahad in transmission but its meaning is clear (qat'i dalala).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'عشر' (ten) explicitly sets the amount. The general phrase 'كل اصبع' (every finger) indicates all fingers of hands and feet are included.
Hanafi usul treats the general (amm) as binding unless specified otherwise.
4
Appreciate the rational argument (qiyas jali)
The text adds a rational basis: cutting all ten fingers of either hands or feet destroys the entire benefit (grasping or walking), thus full diyah is due. Since there are ten fingers, each gets one-tenth.
This is not a separate proof but a supporting reasoning (talil).
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school treats all fingers equally. Some other schools differentiate (e.g., by finger type or joint count). The Hanafi view is mufta bihi.
The difference stems from how the general hadith is interpreted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وفي كل اصبع من اصابع اليدين والرجلين عشر الدية لقوله عليه السلام فى كل اصبع عشر من الابل ولان فى قطع الكل تقويت جنس المنفعة وفيه دية كاملة وهى عشر فتنقسم الدية عليها ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور دونوں ہاتھوں اور دونوں پیروں کی انگلیوں میں سے ہر انگلی میں دیت کا عشر ہے نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے ہر انگلی میں دس اونٹ ہیں اور اس لئے کہ تمام انگلیوں کے کاٹنے میں جنس منفعت کی تعمیل ہے اور اس میں ( تفویت جنس منفعت میں ) پوری دیت ہے۔ اور انگلیاں دس ہیں تو دیت انگلیوں پر منقسم ہوگی۔ تشریح ایک ہاتھ میں پانچ انگلیاں ہیں اور دو میں دس اور اسی طرح دونوں پیروں میں دس اور دونوں ہاتھوں میں یا ان کی دسوں انگلیوں میں پوری دیت واجب ہوتی ہے اور ہر انگلی تمام ہاتھوں کی انگلی کا عشر ہیں لہذا ہر انگلی میں پوری دیت کا عشرہ ۱/ اواجب ہوگا۔ باقی واضح ہے۔
He said: And in every finger of the fingers of the hands and feet is one-tenth of the diyah, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'In every finger, ten camels,' and because in cutting all, the strengthening of the type of benefit [is lost] and in it is a complete diyah, and they are ten, so the diyah is divided upon them.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage establishes the diyah for each finger of both hands and feet. The Shaikh cites the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that each finger incurs ten camels, which is equivalent to one-tenth of the full diyah of 100 camels. The reasoning is that cutting all ten fingers of either hands or feet results in the loss of the entire benefit (grasping or walking), thus full diyah is due, and since there are ten fingers, each gets one-tenth. The Urdu commentary confirms that each finger, whether of hand or foot, is treated equally.

Key Terms
اصبع (isba'): finger (of hand or foot)
دية (diyah): blood money; fixed compensation for bodily harm
عشر (‘ushr): one-tenth

All Fingers Are Equal in Diyah
Ruling establishing equality of all fingers in diyah amount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the diyah of fingers and explain the proof from the generality of the hadith and the equality of benefit.

Core Idea
All fingers are equal in diyah because the hadith is general and they share the same primary benefit.

In this passage, Al-Marghinani concludes a discussion on the diyah (blood money) for fingers by establishing a key Hanafi principle: all fingers—whether of hand or foot, right or left, thumb or pinky—are equal in value. This ruling is based on the general wording of the hadith and the underlying rationale that all fingers serve the same essential benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the diyah for fingers: all fingers are equal in value. The hukm is that each finger carries a diyah of one-tenth of the full diyah (10 camels or equivalent).
This applies to both hands and feet.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith 'في كل اصبع عشر من الابل' (for every finger, ten camels). The hadith is ahad but accepted in this context.
The hadith is cited without reference, but it is well-known in the books of diyat.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The generality of 'كل اصبع' (every finger) indicates that all fingers are included without distinction. Additionally, the text argues that all fingers are equal in their primary benefit (grasping for hands, walking for feet), so no differentiation is justified.
The analogy of right vs. left hand is used to show that differences in utility do not affect diyah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) differentiate between fingers, assigning a higher diyah to the thumb or index finger based on other hadith or analogy.
The Hanafi position rejects such differentiation.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the absolute wording of the hadith and the principle of equal primary benefit. This is the mufta bihi position.
Tarjih authority: This is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, and later Hanafi scholars uphold it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والاصابع كلها سواء لاطلاق الحديث ولانها سواء فى اصل لمنفعة فلا تعتبر الزيادة فيه كاليمين مع الشمال وكذا اصابع الرجلين لانه يفوت بقطع كلها منفعة المشى فتجب الدية كاملة ثم فيهما عشر أصابع فتنقسم الدية عليها اعشارا. ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور تمام انگلیاں برابر ہیں حدیث کے مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اسلئے کہ اصل منفعت کے اندر تمام انگلیاں برابر ہیں تو اس میں زیادتی معتبر نہ ہوگی جیسے داہنا بائیں کے ساتھ اور ایسے ہی دونوں پیروں کی انگلیاں اس لئے کہ ان تمام کے کاٹنے سے چلنے کی منفعت فوت ہو جائے گی تو کامل دیت واجب ہو گی۔ پھر ان دونوں میں ( ہاتھوں اور پیروں میں ) دس انگلیاں ہیں پس دیت دسوں انگلیوں پروس حصے ہو کہ منقسم ہوگی ۔ تشریح جونسی انگلی ہو سب کا حکم برابر ہے کیونکہ جو حدیث اس سے پہلے انگلیوں کے بارے میں مذکور ہوئی وہ مطلق ہے اور اصل پکڑنے کی منفعت میں سب انگلیاں برابر ہیں ۔ تو ان میں کمی زیادتی معتبر نہ ہوگی، جیسے دائیں اور بائیں ہاتھ میں کچھ تفاوت شمار نہیں کیا گیا ہے۔
He said: And the fingers, all of them, are equal, due to the absoluteness of the hadith, and because they are equal in the principle of benefit, so increase is not considered, like the right [hand] with the left. Similarly the fingers of the feet, because by cutting all of them, the benefit of walking is lost, so full diyah becomes obligatory. Then in them are ten fingers, so the diyah is divided upon them into tenths.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage further explains that all fingers – whether of hands or feet, right or left, thumb or pinky – are equal in diyah. The reason is that the hadith about fingers is general (mutlaq) without distinguishing between different fingers. Additionally, all fingers are equal in their essential benefit: all fingers of the hand contribute to grasping, and all toes contribute to walking. Therefore, no finger is given a higher or lower diyah. This is analogous to the right and left hand being equal. The Urdu commentary emphasizes that the prior hadith is absolute, and in terms of primary benefit, all are equivalent.

Key Terms
اصابع (asabi'): plural of finger; includes both hand and foot digits
اطلاق الحديث (itlaq al-hadith): the absoluteness/generality of the hadith, meaning it does not specify any particular finger
منفعة (manfa'ah): benefit; here the primary function of grasping (hand) or walking (foot)

Diyah for Finger Joints: Proportional Division
Ruling on diyah for each finger joint

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah for each joint of a finger based on the number of joints and explain the qiyas that establishes this ruling.

Core Idea
The diyah for a finger joint is proportional to the number of joints: one-third for three-joint fingers, half for two-joint thumbs.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific injury: cutting off a single joint of a finger. It provides a clear ruling based on analogical reasoning, showing how the Hanafi school extends the principle of proportional division from the hand to individual fingers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the injury types
Distinguish between fingers with three joints (index, middle, ring, little) and the thumb with two joints. The ruling differs based on this anatomical difference.
2
State the diyah fraction for each type
For a three-joint finger, one joint incurs one-third of that finger's diyah. For the two-joint thumb, one joint incurs one-half of the thumb's diyah.
3
Identify the asl (original case)
The original ruling is the division of the full hand diyah (5000 dirhams) equally among the five fingers, each receiving 1000 dirhams.
4
Identify the far (new case)
The new case is the division of a single finger's diyah onto its multiple joints.
5
Confirm the illah (effective cause)
The illah is the need for proportional division based on the number of parts (fingers or joints). Both cases involve distributing a fixed total over equal parts.
This is a clear (jali) qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و فى كل اصبع فيها ثلثة مفاصل ففي احدها ثلث دية الاصبع و ما فيها مفصلان ففى احدهما نصف دية الاصبع وهو نظير انقسام دية اليد على الاصابع ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور ہر اس انگلی میں تین جوڑ ہوں تو ایک جوڑ میں انگلی کی دیت کا ثلث ہوگا اور وہ انگلی جس میں دو جوڑ ہوں تو ایک جوڑ میں انگلی کی دیت کا نصف ہوگا اور یہ انگلیوں پر ہاتھ کی دیت منقسم ہونے کی نظیر ہے۔ تشریح کسی انگلی میں تین جوڑ ہوتے ہیں (پورے ) اور انگوٹھے میں دو ہوتے ہیں تو جس انگلی کے پورے تین ہوں اگر اس کا ایک پور کاٹ دیا جائے تو اس میں انگلی کی دیت کا ثلث واجب ہو گا اور جس میں دو پور ہوتے ہیں اگر اس کا ایک پور کاٹ دیا جائے تو اس میں انگلی کی دیت کا نصف واجب ہوگا جیسے ہاتھ کی دیت انگلیوں پر منقسم ہوتی ہے ( کمامر ) ایسے ہی انگلی کی دیت پوروں پر منقسم ہوگی ۔
He said: And in every finger in which there are three joints, in one of them is one-third of the diyah of the finger; and that in which there are two joints, in one of them is half of the diyah of the finger; and it is analogous to the division of the diyah of the hand over the fingers.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for diyah when a specific joint (finger bone) is cut. Fingers with three joints (all except the thumb) incur one-third of that finger's diyah if one joint is cut. The thumb has only two joints, so cutting one joint incurs half of the thumb's diyah. The reasoning is analogical: just as the full diyah of the hand is divided equally among the five fingers, here the diyah of a finger is divided proportionally among its joints. The Urdu commentary clarifies that this division mirrors the division of hand diyah onto fingers.

Key Terms
مفصل (mufsal): joint or phalanx of a finger
دية الاصبع (diyat al-isba'): diyah of one finger
نظير (nadhir): analogue; similar case used for qiyas

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person cuts one joint of the thumb (which has two joints), what fraction of the thumb's diyah is due?
A) One-third
B) One-half
C) One-fourth
D) Full diyah

Key Takeaway
The diyah for a finger joint is a fraction of the finger's diyah, determined proportionally by the number of joints: one-third for three-joint fingers, half for two-joint thumbs.

Each Tooth Incurs Five Camels in Diyah
Ruling on diyah for each tooth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah for each tooth according to the Hanafi school, explain why all teeth are equal in diyah, and distinguish between accidental and intentional tooth injury.

Core Idea
Every tooth, whether incisor or molar, incurs a fixed diyah of five camels when broken accidentally.

In Hanafi law, injury to a tooth – whether front or back – carries a specific compensation (diyah). This lesson examines the ruling from Al-Hidayah, its proof from the hadith of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and the reasoning behind the equality of all teeth. Understanding this ruling clarifies how the school derives fixed compensations for bodily injuries and reinforces the principle that classification by primary benefit overrides differences in appearance or function.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the accidental breaking of a tooth. The ruling (hukm) is that five camels become wajib (obligatory) as diyah for each tooth.
The term 'سن' (sinn) includes all teeth, not just incisors.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari where the Prophet ﷺ said: 'وفى كل سن خمس من الابل' – 'And in every tooth, five camels.' This is a Sunnah ahad hadith transmitted with reliable chains.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalalah due to explicit wording.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'خمس من الابل' directly sets the amount. The word 'كل' (every) indicates generality, covering all types of teeth, which the Hanafi school treats as absolute (mutlaq) and not subject to differentiation.
The hadith is quoted as 'وفى كل سن خمس من الابل' in this passage.
4
Note the equality argument
The passage adds another proof: all teeth are equal in their primary benefit (chewing), so differentiation is not considered – just as all fingers and hands are equal in diyah despite differences in size or function.
This analogy (qiyas) strengthens the ruling that incisors and molars carry the same diyah.
5
Distinguish accidental from intentional
The ruling applies only when the injury is accidental (khata'). If the tooth was broken intentionally ('amd), then qisas (retaliation) applies, not diyah, as already established in the chapter on crimes (Kitab al-Jinayat).
This exception is crucial: diyah is only for unintentional harm; intentional harm triggers a different legal regime.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و في كل سن خمس من الابل لقوله عليه السلام في حديث أبي موسى الاشعرى رضى الله عنه و في كل سن خمس من الابل والاسنان والاضراس سواء لاطلاق ما روينا و لما روى فى بعض الروايات والاسنان كلها سواء ولان كلها فى اصل المنفعة سواء فلا يعتبر التفاضل كالايدى والاصابع وهذا اذا كان خطاء فان كان عماد ففيه القصاص و قد مر فى الجنايات - ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور ہر دانت میں پانچ اونٹ ہیں نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے ابوموسیٰ اشعری کی حدیث میں اور ہر دانت میں پانچ اونٹ ہیں اور دانت اور ڈاڑھ برابر ہیں اس حدیث کے مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم نے روایت کیا ہے اور بعض روایات میں ہے کہ تمام دانت برابر ہیں اور اس لئے کہ تمام دانت اصل منفعت میں برابر ہیں تو تفاضل معتبر نہ ہو گا۔ جیسے ہاتھ اور انگلیاں۔ اور جب ہے کہ کا شناخطاء ہو پس اگر عمد ہو تو آسمیں قصاص ہے اور یہ بحث کتاب الجنایات میں گذر چکی ہے۔ تشریح اگر کسی نے کسی کا دانت توڑ دیا تو ہر دانت میں پانچ اونٹ واجب ہوں گے کیونکہ حدیث میں یونہی وارد ہے۔ پھر دانت ب بر آنہیں خواہ انیاب ہوں یا اضراس ، طواحن ہوں یا نواجذ سب کا حکم ایک ہے اسلئے کہ ابو موسیٰ اشعری کی حدیث میں ، اطلاق ہے۔
He said: And in every tooth: five camels, due to his saying, peace be upon him, in the hadith of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: 'And in every tooth: five camels.' And incisors and molars are equal, due to the absoluteness of what we narrated, and because it is narrated in some narrations: 'And all teeth are equal,' and because they are all equal in the principle of benefit, so differentiation is not considered, like the hands and fingers. And this is when it is accidental; if it is intentional, then there is qisas, and this has passed in [the chapter of] crimes.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for teeth: each tooth, whether front or back, incurs a diyah of five camels. The proof is the hadith of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. The text also notes that all teeth are equal in diyah, because the hadith is absolute (mutlaq) and they share the same primary benefit (chewing). The exception is if the tooth was broken intentionally, in which case qisas (retaliation) applies, not diyah, as previously covered in the chapter on crimes. The Urdu commentary clarifies that all types of teeth – incisors, canines, molars, etc. – are treated equally.

اضراس (adras): molar teeth

عمد ('amd): intentional; deliberate act

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that each tooth, regardless of type, incurs a fixed diyah of five camels when broken accidentally, based on an explicit hadith and the principle of equality in primary benefit.

Full Diyah for Loss of Limb Function
Ruling with proof by talil (causal reasoning)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that full diyah is wajib for total loss of limb function, and distinguish between loss of benefit (manfa'ah) and loss of form (surah).

Core Idea
Full diyah is due for loss of function, not just loss of the limb itself.

This passage from al-Hidayah establishes a key Hanafi rule in diyat: destroying a limb's function triggers the same compensation as destroying the limb itself. The reasoning hinges on the genus of benefit (jins al-manfa'ah). We will unpack the 'illa, examine the examples, and note the exception for self-correcting injuries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The text states: whoever strikes a limb and removes its benefit (manfa'ah) must pay full diyah. This applies even if the limb remains physically intact.
Condition: the loss of benefit must be total, not partial.
2
Understand the 'illa (causal basis)
The author says: 'because what is attached is deprivation of the genus of benefit, not loss of form.' The 'illa is the complete loss of the type of function (jins al-manfa'ah) that the limb provides.
This is a qiyas: loss of limb = full diyah; loss of function = same because 'illa is loss of benefit.
3
Apply to the examples
Paralyzed hand (loss of grip), blind eye (loss of sight), severed reproductive ability (loss of progeny), and hunchback (loss of straight posture) all destroy the genus of benefit, so full diyah is wajib.
Note that the hunchback example adds loss of beauty as a benefit.
4
Note the exception
If the hunchback corrects itself without any lasting effect, no diyah is due because the benefit is restored. Ta'zir (discretionary punishment) may still apply.
This confirms the 'illa: if the benefit returns, the basis for diyah is removed.
5
Relate to cross-madhhab differences
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require actual loss of the limb for full diyah. Hanafis extend to loss of function alone, based on the 'illa of jins al-manfa'ah.
This ikhtilaf arises from different definitions of the effective cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و من عضوا فاذهب منفعته ففيه دية كاملة كاليد اذا شلت والعين اذا ذهب ضوء هالان المتعلق تفویت جنس المنفعة لا قوات الصورة و من ضرب صلب غيره فانقطع ماء وه يجب الدية لتفويت جنس المنفعة وكذا لواحد به لانه فوت جمالا على الكمال وهو الاستواء القامة فلو زالت الهدوية لا شيء عليه لزوالها لا عن اثر -
He said: And whoever strikes a limb and removes its benefit, then full diyah is due, like the hand when it becomes paralyzed, and the eye when its light goes, because what is attached (to full diyah) is the deprivation of the genus of benefit, not the loss of form. And whoever strikes the back of another so that his water (semen) is cut off, full diyah is due for depriving the genus of benefit. And likewise if he makes him hunchbacked, because he destroyed beauty completely, and that is straightness of stature. So if the hunchback goes away, nothing is due due to its going away without effect.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof by talil (causal reasoning). The author explains that full diyah is obligatory when a limb's function (manfa'ah) is destroyed, even if the limb itself remains intact. The principle is that the basis for full diyah is the loss of the genus of benefit (jins al-manfa'ah), not the loss of the physical form (surah). Examples: a paralyzed hand, a blind eye, loss of reproductive ability, or being made hunchbacked (which destroys straight posture). However, if the hunchback corrects itself without any lasting effect, no diyah is owed, but ta'zir (discretionary punishment) may be applied. This ruling applies in cases of khatta' (accidental injury); in 'amd (intentional) cases, qisas may apply.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money, a fixed monetary compensation paid to the victim or his heirs for bodily injury or homicide.
جنس المنفعة (jins al-manfa'ah): The genus or category of benefit derived from a limb, such as sight for the eye, grip for the hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Loss of the physical form of the limb
B) Loss of the genus of benefit (jins al-manfa'ah)
C) The pain caused to the victim
D) The intention of the attacker

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that full diyah is wajib for total loss of limb function because the 'illa is loss of the genus of benefit, not loss of the physical limb.

The Six Types of Shijaj: Definitions and Distinctions
Defining six categories of head wounds from al-Quduri's matn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define each of the six shijaj types and distinguish them based on blood presence and wound depth.

Core Idea
Head wound classification determines diyah – each type has a prescribed compensation.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar defines six of the ten recognized head wounds (shijaj). These definitions form the foundation for diyat rulings: the type of wound directly determines the amount of blood money. Understanding these categories is essential for correctly assessing injury severity and applying Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six types listed
Read the Arabic passage and list the six terms mentioned: al-harisah, al-dami'ah, al-damiyah, al-badi'ah, al-mutalahimah, al-simhaq. Note that the passage says 'ten' but only describes these six.
The remaining four types (e.g., al-mudihah, al-hashimah) are covered later.
2
Extract the defining feature of each type
For each term, identify the key descriptor: al-harisah scratches without blood; al-dami'ah shows blood but doesn't flow; al-damiyah causes flow; al-badi'ah cuts skin; al-mutalahimah penetrates flesh; al-simhaq reaches the membrane over the skull.
Focus on the presence/absence of blood and depth of penetration.
3
Create a severity continuum
Arrange the six types from least to most severe: al-harisah (mildest) → al-dami'ah → al-damiyah → al-badi'ah → al-mutalahimah → al-simhaq (deepest listed).
This ordering helps in assigning diyat amounts (not covered here).
4
Distinguish al-dami'ah and al-damiyah
Note that al-dami'ah only shows blood (tears-like) while al-damiyah actually flows. This is a common point of confusion; the passage uses 'like tears' as an analogy.
The difference is blood flow, not visible presence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشجاج عشرة الحارصة وهى التى تحرص الجلداى تخدشه ولا تخرج الدم والدامعة وهي التي تظهر الدم ولا تسيله كالدمع فى العين والدامية وهى التى تسيل الدم والباضعة وهى التى تبضع الجلداى تقطعه والمتلاحمة وهى التى تأخذ في اللحم والسمحاق وهي جلدة رقيقة بين اللحم وعظم الراس
He said: Al-shijaj are ten. Al-harisah: it is that which scratches the skin, cutting it without drawing blood. Al-dami'ah: it is that which shows blood but does not let it flow, like tears in the eye. Al-damiyah: it is that which makes blood flow. Al-badi'ah: it is that which cuts the skin. Al-mutalahimah: it is that which penetrates into the flesh. Al-simhaq: it is a thin membrane between the flesh and the skull bone.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This is a definitional passage from the matn of al-Quduri, listing six of the ten types of shijaj (head/face wounds). The commentary (Sharh) explains each term: al-harisah is a superficial scratch without blood; al-dami'ah shows blood but does not flow; al-damiyah causes blood to flow; al-badi'ah cuts the skin; al-mutalahimah penetrates deeper into the flesh; al-simhaq reaches the thin membrane covering the skull. These definitions establish the categories for subsequent rulings on diyat for head wounds, as each type has a prescribed amount (arsh). The remaining four types (not mentioned here) include the ones that reach the bone or break it, which are covered later.

Key Terms
الشجاج (al-shijaj): Plural of shajjah; wounds that occur on the head or face.
الحارصة (al-harisah): A wound that scratches the skin without drawing blood.
الدامعة (al-dami'ah): A wound that shows blood but does not let it flow.
الدامية (al-damiyah): A wound that causes blood to flow.
الباضعة (al-badi'ah): A wound that cuts the skin and flesh, but not deeply.
المتلاحمة (al-mutalahimah): A wound that penetrates deeply into the flesh.
السمحاق (al-simhaq): A thin membrane between the flesh and the skull bone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Al-harisah
B) Al-dami'ah
C) Al-damiyah
D) Al-badi'ah

Key Takeaway
The six types of shijaj are distinguished by the presence or absence of blood flow and the depth of the wound, forming a continuum from a scratch to the membrane covering the skull.

The Ten Types of Head Wounds (Shijaj) Defined
Listing and defining the ten types of head wounds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the ten types of head wounds (shijaj) in order of severity, define each type, and identify which type permits qisas (retaliation) in Hanafi law.

Core Idea
Head wounds are classed by depth; only al-mudihah allows qisas because the bone is exposed equally.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn systematically defines the ten head wounds (shijaj) that form the basis for diyat (blood money) and qisas. Understanding these precise definitions is essential for applying the correct legal consequences. The Urdu commentary clarifies subtle distinctions between similar-looking wounds.

Guided Path
1
1. Grasp the scope of shijaj
Recognise that shijaj are wounds limited to the head and face, distinct from jurh (wounds elsewhere). This classification affects diyat and qisas rules.
The Arabic term شجاج is plural of شجة.
2
2. Learn the first three wounds by blood flow
Al-harisah (scratch, no blood), al-dami'ah (blood appears but does not flow), al-damiyah (blood flows). These are the mildest, involving only skin.
The Urdu commentary emphasises that in the latter two the skin is cut even though the definitions focus on blood.
3
3. Learn wounds that cut skin and flesh
Al-badi'ah (skin cut), al-mutalahimah (penetrates flesh), al-simhaq (reaches the thin membrane between flesh and skull). These involve deeper tissue but not bone.
Al-simhaq is the last wound before bone is affected.
4
4. Understand the four wounds affecting bone
Al-mudihah (bone exposed), al-hashimah (bone broken), al-munaqqilah (bone displaced), al-ammah (reaches brain covering). Severity increases from bone exposure to brain involvement.
Al-mudihah is the only one where qisas applies because the injury can be matched exactly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الشجاج
قال الشجاج عشرة: الحارصة وهي التي تحرص الجلد أي تخدشه ولا تخرج الدم، والدامعة وهي التي تظهر الدم ولا تسيله كالدمع في العين، والدامية وهي التي تسيل الدم، والباضعة وهي التي تبضع الجلد أي تقطعه، والمتلاحمة وهي التي تأخذ في اللحم، والسمحاق وهي جلدة رقيقة بين اللحم وعظم الرأس. والموضحة وهي التي توضح العظم أي تبينه، والهاشمة وهي التي تكسر العظم، والمنقلة وهي التي تنقل العظم بعد الكسر أي تحوله، والآمة وهي التي تصل إلى أم الرأس وهو الذي فيه الدماغ.
تشريح: سر اور چہرہ کے چھ زخموں کا بیان آگیا ہے۔ حارصہ میں فقط کھال میں خراش ہوتی ہے۔ دامعہ میں خون دکھائی تو دیتا ہے مگر بہتا نہیں ہے۔ دامیہ جس میں خون بہہ جائے۔ باضعہ جس میں گوشت کٹ جائے۔ متلاحمہ جس میں گوشت کٹ جائے یعنی گوشت میں گھس جائے۔ اسحاق گوشت اور سر کی ہڈی کے درمیان ایک باریک سی جھلی ہے جب زخم اس جھلی تک پہنچ جائے تو اسے اسحاق کہتے ہیں۔
موضحہ، ہاشمہ، منقلہ اور آمہ کا بیان:
تشریح: اس عبارت میں مابقی چار زخموں کا ذکر ہے۔ موضحہ جس میں ہڈی کھل جائے اور ظاہر ہو جائے۔ ہاشمہ جس میں ہڈی ٹوٹ جائے۔ منقلہ جس میں ہڈی ٹوٹ کر اپنی جگہ سے سرک جائے۔ آمہ زخم ام الراس تک پہنچ جائے اور ام الراس وہ ہے جس میں بھیجا رہتا ہے۔
Section on Head Wounds. He (al-Quduri) said: Head wounds are ten: al-harisah, which scratches the skin without causing blood to flow; al-dami'ah, which makes blood appear but does not flow like tears; al-damiyah, which makes blood flow; al-badi'ah, which cuts the skin; al-mutalahimah, which penetrates the flesh; al-simhaq, which is a thin membrane between flesh and skull. al-mudihah, which lays bare the bone; al-hashimah, which breaks the bone; al-munaqqilah, which displaces the bone after breakage; al-ammah, which reaches the membrane covering the brain (umm al-ra's). Commentary: The description of the six wounds of the head and face has come. In harisah there is only a scratch on the skin. In dami'ah blood appears but does not flow. In damiyah blood flows. In badi'ah the flesh is cut. In mutalahimah the wound penetrates the flesh. Simhaq is a thin membrane between flesh and skull bone; when the wound reaches this membrane it is called simhaq. Section on Mudihah, Hashimah, Munaqqilah and Ammah: Commentary: In this passage the remaining four wounds are mentioned. Mudihah: the bone is exposed and visible. Hashimah: the bone is broken. Munaqqilah: the bone is broken and displaced from its position. Ammah: the wound reaches umm al-ra's, which contains the brain.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a definition_ruling that enumerates and defines the ten types of head wounds (shijaj) in Hanafi diyat law. The author, al-Quduri, lists them in order of severity. The first six are superficial: harisah (scratch without blood), dami'ah (blood appears but does not flow), damiyah (blood flows), badi'ah (skin cut), mutalahimah (flesh cut), simhaq (reaches the membrane). The last four are more severe: mudihah (bone exposed), hashimah (bone broken), munaqqilah (bone displaced), ammah (reaches the brain covering). The Urdu commentary explains each term and clarifies that simhaq is a thin membrane between flesh and skull. It also notes that in three of the first six (harisah, dami'ah, damiyah) the skin is cut despite the definitions focusing on other aspects. This classification is foundational for determining diyat (blood money) amounts and the applicability of qisas (retaliation).

Key Terms
شجاج (shijāj): Plural of shajjah, meaning wounds specifically on the head or face.
موضحہ (mūḍiḥah): A wound that exposes the bone by cutting through the flesh and membrane.
آمہ (āmmah): A wound that reaches the membrane covering the brain (umm al-ra's).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) al-hashimah
C) al-mudihah
D) al-simhaq

Key Takeaway
The ten head wounds (shijaj) are defined by depth of tissue involvement: from skin scratch to brain membrane; only al-mudihah allows qisas because of exact equivalence.

Qisas for Al-Mudihah and Its Limitation to Other Head Wounds
Establishing qisas for al-mudihah and denying it for other shijaj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for head wounds, identify the two proofs for qisas in al-mudihah, and explain why qisas is not applicable to other shijaj.

Core Idea
Qisas for head wounds is only valid for al-mudihah because precise equality is achievable only there.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar on the law of qisas for head wounds. The passage establishes that qisas applies exclusively to al-mudihah (the wound that bares the bone) when intentional, and denies it for all other categories of shijaj. The justification combines a textual proof (hadith) with a rational argument based on the feasibility of exact equality (musawah). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying retaliation law and avoiding overreach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage explicitly states that qisas applies for intentional mudihah and does not apply for other head wounds. Note the exception: only mudihah qualifies.
The ruling is specific to intentional ('amdan) acts.
2
Examine the naqli proof (hadith)
The author cites a hadith from al-Bayhaqi: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) decreed qisas for al-mudihah.' This serves as direct textual evidence.
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the aqli proof (possibility of equality)
In mudihah, the knife can reach the bone and stop, allowing a precisely equal cut in retaliation. This ensures musawah (equality).
The rational argument is based on the natural limit provided by the bone.
4
Apply the illa to deeper wounds
For wounds above mudihah (e.g., hashimah, munaqqilah, ammah), there is bone-breaking. For shallower wounds (e.g., harisah), there is no fixed depth. In both cases, exact equality is impossible.
Bone-breaking cannot be replicated precisely; shallow wounds have no natural stopping point.
5
State the consequence
For non-mudihah wounds, qisas is not permitted; instead, the perpetrator pays compensation (diyah or hukumat al-'adl).
This preserves justice without risking excessive retaliation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ففى الموضحة القصاص ان كانت عمدا لما روى انه عليه السلام قضى بالقصاص في الموضحة ولانه يمكن ان ينتهى السكين الى العظم فيتساويان فيتحقق المساوات.
قال ولا قصاص في بقية الشجاج لانه لا يمكن اعتبار المساواة فيها لانه لاحد ينتهى السكين اليه ولان فيما فوق الموضحة كسر العظم ولا قصاص فيه.
ترجمہ: قدوری نے فرمایا پس موضحہ میں قصاص ہے اگر وہ عمد ہو۔ بوجہ اس کے کہ مروی ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے موضحہ میں قصاص کا فیصلہ فرمایا۔ اور اس لئے کہ ممکن ہے کہ ہڈی تک چھری پہنچے پس دونوں برابر ہو جائیں گے پس مساوات متحقق ہو جائے گی۔ اور بقیہ شجاج میں قصاص نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ ان میں مساوات کا اعتبار کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ کوئی ایسی حد نہیں ہے جس حد پر جا کر چھری رک جائے۔ اور اس لئے کہ ان زخموں میں جو موضحہ سے بڑھ کر ہیں ہڈی کو توڑنا ہے اور ہڈی کو توڑنے میں قصاص نہیں ہے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: So for al-mudihah, there is qisas if it was intentional, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) decreed qisas for al-mudihah, and because it is possible for the knife to reach the bone, so the two (wounds) become equal, thus equality is achieved. He said: And there is no qisas in the rest of the head wounds, because it is not possible to consider equality in them, because there is no limit at which the knife stops, and because in wounds above al-mudihah there is breaking of the bone, and there is no qisas in bone-breaking.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling_with_proof on the applicability of qisas (retaliation) for head wounds. The matn states that qisas is established for al-mudihah (the wound that exposes the bone) if it is intentional ('amdan). Two proofs are given: first, a hadith from al-Bayhaqi that the Prophet (ﷺ) judged qisas for al-mudihah; second, a rational argument that in al-mudihah the wound stops at the bone, so the knife can be used to cut exactly to the bone in retaliation, achieving the required equality (musawah). For all other types of shijaj (the remaining nine), qisas is not applicable. The reason given is that equality cannot be ensured: for the less severe wounds (like harisah) there is no fixed depth where a knife can stop, and for the more severe wounds (hashimah, munaqqilah, ammah) there is bone-breaking, and qisas is not prescribed for breaking bones due to the risk of excess and harm. The legal consequence is that for non-mudihah head wounds, the guilty party must pay compensation (hukumat al-'adl or diyat) instead of undergoing qisas.

Key Terms
قصاص (qiṣāṣ): Retaliation in kind, specifically for wounds where exact equality is possible.
موضحہ (mūḍiḥah): A wound that exposes the bone by cutting through flesh and membrane.
مساوات (musāwāt): Equality between the inflicted wound and the retaliatory wound in terms of location, depth, and nature.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is qisas not applicable to head wounds deeper than mudihah (e.g., hashimah)?
A) Because there is no hadith mentioning them
B) Because equality cannot be achieved due to the lack of a fixed stopping point
C) Because those wounds are considered minor
D) Because the victim always dies from them

Key Takeaway
Qisas for head wounds is limited to intentional mudihah because only that wound allows exact equality in retaliation; all other shijaj require compensation instead.

Head Wounds and Qisas for Mudihah
Defines four head wounds and rules qisas for intentional mudihah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the four head wounds and state the ruling of qisas for intentional mudihah with its evidence.

Core Idea
Only the mudihah wound qualifies for qisas because exact equality in cutting to the bone is achievable.

In this lesson, we study four of the ten head wounds (shijaj) and their legal consequences. The Hanafi school distinguishes the mudihah from other wounds because qisas (retaliation) applies when the perpetrator can receive an identical wound. The passage from al-Quduri's matn, with commentary, defines each wound and provides the proof for qisas on mudihah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is intentionally inflicting a mudihah wound. The ruling is that qisas is wajib (obligatory).
The text states 'fī al-mūḍiḥati al-qiṣāṣu in kānat ʿamdan.'
2
Locate the first dalil
A hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) decreed qisas for mudihah. This is a naqli proof.
The hadith is ahad, making its thubut zanni, but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the second dalil (aql)
Equality (musawa) is possible because the knife can reach the bone, allowing an identical wound to be inflicted.
For other wounds, equality is impossible (e.g., bone cannot be re-broken equally).
4
Note the scope of the ruling
Qisas is ONLY for mudihah, not for hashimah, munaqqilah, ammah, or other head wounds.
For those, compensation is either 'arsh (fixed) or hukumat al-adl (equitable).
5
Confirm the Hanafi tarjih
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and relied upon by later Hanafi authorities like al-Marghinani.
No intra-madhhab ikhtilaf among Hanafis on this specific point.

Al-Mudihah: it is that which exposes the bone, i.e., makes it visible. Al-Hashimah: it is that which breaks the bone. Al-Munaqqilah: it is that which shifts the bone after breaking, i.e., moves it. Al-Ammah: it is that which reaches the 'umm al-ra's (membrane covering the brain). He (al-Quduri) said: So for mudihah, qisas applies if it was intentional, because of the report that the Prophet (peace be upon him) decreed qisas for mudihah, and because it is possible for the knife to reach the bone, so they become equal, thus equality is realized.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It defines four of the ten types of head wounds (shijaj): al-mudihah (which exposes the bone), al-hashimah (which breaks the bone), al-munaqqilah (which shifts the bone after breaking), and al-ammah (which reaches the brain membrane). The author then states that if mudihah is intentional, qisas (retaliation) is obligatory. Two proofs are given: (1) a hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) decreed qisas for mudihah, and (2) rational reasoning that equality (musawa) is possible because the knife can stop at the bone, allowing the exact same wound to be inflicted. For all other head wounds (the remaining nine), qisas is not applicable; instead, 'arsh (fixed compensation) or hukumat al-adl (equitable compensation) is given.

Key Terms
الموضحة (al-mudihah): A wound that exposes the bone, making it visible.
الهاشمة (al-hashimah): A wound that breaks the bone.
المنقلة (al-munaqqilah): A wound that shifts the bone from its place after breaking.
الآمة (al-ammah): A wound that reaches the membrane covering the brain (umm al-ra's).
القصاص (al-qisas): Legal retaliation: inflicting an equivalent wound or injury on the perpetrator.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Qisas for Head Wounds Before Mudihah
States the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on qisas for minor head wounds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas for wounds before mudihah and apply the method of musawah (equality) to determine qisas applicability.

Core Idea
Qisas requires exact equality; for wounds before mudihah, Zahir al-Riwayah allows it by measured depth, while a weak narration denies it.

In Hanafi law, qisas (retaliation) is only permitted when exact equality (musawah) can be achieved. This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the six head wounds that are less severe than mudihah (the wound that exposes the bone). The Zahir al-Riwayah, represented by Imam Muhammad, holds that qisas is wajib because the depth can be measured precisely. However, a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa (transmitted by Hasan ibn Ziyad) rejects qisas for these wounds. We will explore the reasoning and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wounds in question
Recognize the six shijaj before mudihah (e.g., kharsh, bazi', etc.) that are flesh wounds without bone exposure.
These are distinct from the three wounds after mudihah (hāshimah, munqilah, āmmah) which involve bone break.
2
State the two positions
Position A: No qisas (Imam Abu Hanifa's narration via Hasan ibn Ziyad). Position B: Qisas wajib (Imam Muhammad’s view in al-Asl, which is Zahir al-Riwayah).
The disagreement is only for the first six; all agree no qisas for the last three.
3
Analyze the basis of each position
Position A argues equality (musawah) is impossible because there is no fixed limit. Position B argues equality is possible since only soft tissue is involved and depth can be measured.
The key condition for qisas is the ability to achieve exact retaliation without excess.
4
Learn the method to ensure equality
Use a probe (misbar) to measure the depth of the wound, then sharpen a blade to exactly that depth and cut precisely the same amount.
This technical method satisfies the requirement of musawah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and reasoning
The commentator and al-Zayla'i hold that Zahir al-Riwayah is the correct position (asah) and it is the relied-upon view. The other narration is considered weak.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the transmission and the feasibility of equality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

چھری ٹھہر جائے یہ دلیل تو سب کے لئے عام ہے۔ اور موضحہ کے بعد جن تین کا ذکر ہے یعنی ہاشمہ منقلہ ، آمہ کا ان میں قصاص نہ ہونے کی وجہ یہ بھی ہے کہ ان سب میں ہڈی ٹوٹتی ہے اور ماقبل میں مسئلہ گزرچکا ہے کہ ہڈیوں میں قصاص نہیں ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام امام ابو حنیفہ کی اس روایت کے مطابق موضحہ سے اوپر جو چھ مذکور ہیں نہ ان میں قصاص ہے اور نہ ان تین میں جو موضحہ کے بعد مذکور ہیں۔ ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق موضحہ سے پہلے حديدة بقدر ذالك فيقطع بها مقدار ما قطع فيتحقق استيفاء القصاص ترجمہ اور یہ ایک روایت ہے ابوحنیفہ سے اور محمد نے مبسوط میں فرمایا ہے اور یہی ظاہر الروایہ ہے کہ ان زخموں میں جو موضحہ سے پہلے ہیں قصاص الروایہ ہے اور دوسری طرف امام ابو حنیفہ کی ایک روایت ہے کہ ان میں بھی قصاص نہ ہوگا ( کمامر ) اور ظاہر الروایہ یہ ہے کہ جس کو امام محمد نے مبسوط میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ موضحہ سے پہلے جن چھ زخموں کا ذکر ہے ان میں قصاص لیا جائے گا کیونکہ یہاں ہڈی تو ٹوٹی نہیں ہے اور ایسے معمولی زخموں سے خوف ہلاکت بھی غالب نہیں ہے البدایہاں مساوات ہوسکتی ہے۔ اور مساوات کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ ایک سلائی سے زخم کی گہرائی کی پیمائش کر لی جائے جتنی اس کی گہرائی ہو اتنا ہی بڑا تیز دھار والا لوہا لے کر اتنا ہی کاٹ دیا جائے جتنا اس کا کٹا ہوا ہے لہذا مساوات ہوگئی۔ 1- تنبیہ امام اول بین زیاد نے روایت کیا میں امام صاحب سے قول اول کو حسن بن زیاد نے روایت کیا ہے گر خظاہر الروایہ میں قصاص واجب ہوگا اور اصح یہی ہے۔ زیلعی ص ۱۳۳ ج ۶، سلب الا نبر ص ۵۵۷ ج ۲ ۔ تنبيه - ۲ مگر سمحاق میں بالا جماع قصاص نہ ہو گا جیسے موضحہ سے بعد والے تین میں بالا جماع قصاص نہیں ہے۔ سلب 11 برس ۵۵۷ ج ۲
He said: And there is no qisas in the remaining shijaj because it is not possible to consider equality in them, because there is no limit at which the knife stops, and because in wounds above mudihah there is breaking of bone, and there is no qisas for that. And this is a narration from Abu Hanifa. And Muhammad said in al-Asl, and it is the Zahir al-Riwayah: qisas is obligatory for wounds before mudihah because equality can be considered in them, since there is no breaking of bone and no predominant fear of death. So its depth is measured with a probe, then a piece of iron is sharpened to that measurement, and he cuts with it an amount equal to what he cut, thus the execution of qisas is realized.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding qisas for head wounds that are less severe than mudihah (the first six of the ten shijaj). The matn of al-Quduri states that there is no qisas for the remaining shijaj (i.e., all except mudihah) because equality is impossible: there is no fixed limit for the knife to stop, and wounds above mudihah involve breaking bone, for which qisas is not established. However, the commentator notes a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that even the wounds before mudihah have no qisas. But Imam Muhammad, in his work al-Asl (which is the basis of Zahir al-Riwayah), holds that qisas is obligatory for wounds before mudihah because they involve only flesh and skin; there is no bone break and no predominant fear of death. The method to ensure equality is to measure the wound's depth with a probe, then use a blade of exactly that depth to cut an equal amount. The commentator clarifies that this is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi), and the other narration is weak. Two tanbih (cautions) are added: (1) The first narration from Abu Hanifa was transmitted by Hasan ibn Ziyad, but the correct practice is according to Zahir al-Riwayah. (2) Even for the wound samhaq (which is a type of shajjah reaching the skin over the bone), there is consensus that no qisas applies, just as for the three wounds after mudihah.

Key Terms
الشجاج (al-shijaj): Wounds specific to the head and face; ten types are enumerated in Hanafi fiqh.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The transmitted and authoritative books of the Hanafi school (the six books of Imam Muhammad).
المساواة (al-musawah): Equality or exact equivalence between the original injury and the retaliation.
السمحاق (al-samhaq): A wound that reaches the thin membrane covering the bone (the periosteum).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, what is the method to ensure equality (musawa) when exacting qisas for wounds before mudihah?
A) The victim specifies the depth of the cut
B) A probe measures the wound's depth, then a blade cut to that size is used
C) The offender chooses the depth of retaliation
D) No specific method is required

Key Takeaway
For wounds before mudihah, the Hanafi relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) mandates qisas if exact depth can be matched via probe measurement.

Hukumat al-Adl for Wounds Below Mudihah
Ruling that hukumat al-adl is wajib for wounds below mudihah when qisas is not applied

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of hukumat al-adl for wounds below mudihah, explain the reasoning based on absence of fixed diyah and the dignity of man, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the application of qisas.

Core Idea
When no fixed diyah exists and qisas is inapplicable, equitable compensation (hukumat al-adl) becomes wajib.

In the Hanafi school, the compensation for bodily injuries is determined by either fixed amounts (arsh) or through judge-assessed equitable compensation (hukumat al-adl). This passage from Al-Quduri addresses wounds that are less severe than mudihah (a wound that lays bare the bone). According to one narration, qisas is not applied for such wounds, and no fixed diyah exists. How then should the victim be compensated? Let us follow the legal reasoning of the Hanafi masters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wound and its legal category
First, recognize that the wound in question is below mudihah (not laying bare the bone). According to one narration, qisas is not obligatory for such wounds. We must determine the appropriate compensation.
Mudihah has a fixed arsh of 5% of full diyah. Below mudihah has no fixed amount.
2
State the ruling and its basis
Imam al-Quduri rules that hukumat al-adl (equitable assessment by a judge) is wajib. The basis is twofold: (a) there is no prescribed arsh from the Lawgiver, and (b) the wound cannot be ignored (la yumkin ihdaru) because that would violate human dignity.
The reasoning is that compensation must be just; zero compensation is not an option.
3
Analyze the evidence (dalil)
The passage cites the practice of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and Caliph Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz. Their reports indicate that when no fixed amount exists, a judge determines a fair sum. This is a qawl al-sahabi/tabi'i and is considered zanni in transmission and meaning.
The evidence is not from Quran or Sunnah directly, but from the practice of early authorities.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The commentator clarifies that the correct (mufta bihi) position from Zahir al-Riwayah is that qisas is wajib for wounds below mudihah if they are intentional. Only if one follows a weaker narration (that qisas is not applied) does hukumat al-adl become the Fallback.
Thus the ruling in this passage is conditional on accepting the minority narration.
5
Derive the practical outcome
In practice, the mufta bihi is qisas for intentional wounds below mudihah. However, if qisas is not feasible (e.g., the wound is not intentional), then hukumat al-adl applies. This lesson highlights how Hanafi fiqh provides a fallback mechanism preserving justice.
This shows the school's flexibility in ensuring no injury goes uncompensated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موضحہ سے کم میں حکومت عدل ہے قال وفيما دون الموضحة حكومة العدل لانه ليس فيها ارش مقدر ولا يمكن اهداره فوجب اعتباره بحكم العدل وهو ماثور عن النخعى وعمر بن عبد العزيز . ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور موضحہ سے کم میں حکومت عدل ہے اس لئے کہ ان میں کوئی دیت مقرر نہیں ہے اور نہ اس کا اهدار ممکن ہے تو حکومت عدل کے ذریعہ اس کا اعتبار کرنا واجب ہوا ۔ اور یہی منقول ہے ابراہیم نخعی سے اور عمر بن عبد العزیز ہے۔ تشریح قدوری نے باقی میں فرمایا تھا کہ موضحہ کے علاوہ میں قصاص واجب نہیں ہے مگر ہم عرض کر چکے ہیں کہ صحیح روایت ظاہر الروایہ کی ہے۔ ( کما ) بہر حال جس روایت کے مطابق مادون الموضحہ میں قصاص واجب نہیں ہوا، تو اس میں حکومت عدل واجب ہے یعنی نہ دیت اور نہ قصاص ۔ عدم قصاص کی وجہ تو مذکور ہو چکی ہے، اور عدم دیت کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ شارع کی جانب سے تقدیر نہیں ہے اور اپنے قیاس سے ارش کی مقدار متعین نہیں کی جاسکتی۔ اور یہ بھی نہیں ہوسکتا کہ کچھ بھی واجب نہ ہو اور اس کو ہدر قرار دیا جائے۔ کیونکہ یہ تکریم انسان کے خلاف ہے تو جب کوئی چارہ نہ ملا تو ہم نے مجبوراً حکومت عدل کو اختیار کیا ہے اور یہ حضرت ابراہیم نخعی سے اور عمر بن عبد العزیز سے منقول ہے۔
In wounds below mudihah, hukumat al-adl is applied. Quduri said: 'And in what is below mudihah, hukumat al-adl, because there is no prescribed diyah in them and it cannot be ignored, so it becomes obligatory to assess it by hukumat al-adl. And this is reported from al-Nakha'i and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz.' Translation: Quduri said: In wounds below mudihah, hukumat al-adl is applied because they have no prescribed diyah and it cannot be ignored, so it is obligatory to consider it through hukumat al-adl. This is reported from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz. Commentary: Quduri had said in the remaining that qisas is not obligatory in other than mudihah, but we have stated that the correct narration is Zahir al-Riwayah. However, according to the narration that qisas is not obligatory in below mudihah, then hukumat al-adl is obligatory, i.e., neither diyah nor qisas. The reason for no qisas has been mentioned, and the reason for no diyah is that there is no determination from the Lawgiver, and the amount of arsh cannot be determined by analogy. And it cannot be that nothing is obligated and it is ignored, because that is against the honor of man. So when there is no alternative, we have necessarily adopted hukumat al-adl. And this is reported from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling (hukm) for wounds that are less severe than mudihah (i.e., pre-mudihah wounds) according to the view that qisas is not applied. The author, Imam al-Quduri, states that for such wounds, hukumat al-adl (equitable compensation) is wajib. The reason is that these wounds have no prescribed diyah (fixed blood-money) from the Lawgiver, and they cannot be left uncompensated (ignored) because that would violate the dignity of a human being. Since neither qisas nor a fixed diyah applies, the only option is for a judge to assess an equitable amount based on the severity of the wound, the status of the victim, and other relevant factors. This ruling is supported by the practice of the tabi'in (successors) Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and the caliph Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz. The commentator notes that the correct and relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is actually that qisas is wajib (as per Zahir al-Riwayah), but if one adopts the narration that qisas is not applied, then hukumat al-adl becomes the fallback ruling.

Key Terms
حکومت عدل (hukumat al-adl): Equitable compensation determined by a judge for injuries that have no fixed diyah; an amount assessed based on factors like the wound's severity and the victim's status.
ارش (arsh): Compensation for bodily injury; sometimes used synonymously with diyah for specific wounds, but here refers to prescribed fixed amounts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does hukumat al-adl become wajib for wounds below mudihah?
A) Because the wound has a prescribed diyah but the victim demands more.
B) Because the wound cannot be ignored (la yumkin ihdaru) and has no fixed compensation.
C) Because the wound is intentional (amd).
D) Because the wound is on a sensitive part of the body.

Key Takeaway
When a wound has no fixed compensation and qisas is not applied, equitable compensation (hukumat al-adl) becomes wajib to preserve human dignity.

Fixed Diyah Amounts for Six Specific Wounds in Accidental Cases
Listing prescribed diyah amounts for six types of wounds when accidental

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prescribed diyah fraction for each of the six specific wounds (mudihah, hashimah, munqilah, ammah, ja'ifah, penetrating ja'ifah) in accidental cases.

Core Idea
Six wounds: mudihah 1/20, hashimah 1/10, munqilah 3/20, ammah 1/3, ja'ifah 1/3, penetrating ja'ifah 2/3.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a specific wound is inflicted accidentally (khata), the perpetrator must pay a fixed fraction of the full diyah (blood-money). This lesson anchors the six prescribed amounts as listed in Imam al-Quduri's matn, a foundational text of the school. Memorizing these fractions is essential for accurate compensation in accidental injury cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six wound types
Recognize the Arabic terms: mudihah (exposes bone), hashimah (fractures bone), munqilah (displaces bone), ammah (reaches brain), ja'ifah (penetrates cavity), and penetrating ja'ifah (two openings).
Definitions are standard across schools.
2
Associate each wound with its diyah fraction
Memorize the fixed fraction of full diyah (100 camels) for each: mudihah 1/20 (5 camels), hashimah 1/10 (10 camels), munqilah 3/20 (15 camels), ammah 1/3 (33.33 camels), ja'ifah 1/3, penetrating ja'ifah 2/3.
Fractions can be expressed as camel numbers.
3
Note the condition of accidental (khata)
These amounts apply only when the wound is caused by mistake. For intentional wounds, qisas may take precedence.
The text emphasizes 'if it is khata' for each type.
4
Understand the penetrating ja'ifah special case
If a ja'ifah penetrates through the body, it is counted as two separate wounds, each incurring 1/3, total 2/3 diyah.
This is the only wound with a doubled amount.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موضحہ اگر خطاء ہو تو دیت واجب ہے قال وفى الموضحة ان كانت خطأ نصف عشر الدية وفى الهاشمة عشر الدية وفى المنقلة عشر الدية ونصف عشر الدية وفى الامة ثلث الدية وفى الجائفة ثلث الدية فان نفذت فهما جائفتان ففيهما ثلثا الدية ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور موضحہ میں اگر وہ خطا ہو دیت کے عشر کا نصف (یعنی بیسواں) ہے اور ہاشمہ میں دیت کا عشر ہے اور منقلہ میں دیت کا عشر اور دیت کا نصف عشر ہے اور آمہ میں تہائی دیت ہے اور جائفہ میں تہائی دیت ہے پس اگر جائفہ پار ہو جائے تو یہ دو جائے ہیں پس ان دونوں میں دیت کا دو ثلث واجب ہو گا۔ تشریح ماقبل میں موضحہ کا حکم قصاص کا بیان کیا گیا ہے یہ اس وقت ہے جب کہ یہ زخم عمدہ لگایا گیا ہو اور اگر خطاء ہو تو اس میں دیت واجب ہوگی ۔ جن کی مقدار یہاں بیان کی گئی ہے اور اس کے علاوہ دیگر وہ زخم جن میں دیت واجب ہے وہاں خطاء کی قید ملحوظ نہیں ہے ؟ خطاء دونوں صورتوں میں یہی حکم ہے اب دیت کی تفصیل بیان فرماتے ہیں۔ - موضحہ میں، دیت کا بیسواں حصہ واجب ہوگا یعنی پانچ اونٹ۔ باشمہ میں دیت کا عشر واجب ہوگا یعنی دس اونٹ ۔ - منقلہ میں عشر دیت اور نصف عشر واجب ہوگا یعنی پندرہ اونٹ ۔
In mudihah, if it is khata, half of one-tenth of diyah (i.e., 1/20). In hashimah, one-tenth of diyah. In munqilah, one-tenth plus half of one-tenth (i.e., 15/100 = 3/20). In ammah, one-third of diyah. In ja'ifah, one-third of diyah. If it penetrates through (naufadh), then there are two ja'ifas and in them two-thirds of diyah. Commentary: Previously the ruling of qisas for mudihah was discussed when it is intentional. If it is khata, then diyah is wajib. The amounts are given here. For other wounds where diyah is wajib, the condition of khata is not considered. In both cases the same ruling applies. Now the details of diyah: Mudihah: 1/20 = 5 camels. Hashimah: 1/10 = 10 camels. Munqilah: 1/10 + 1/20 = 15 camels.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage presents a straightforward listing (matn) from Imam al-Quduri regarding the fixed diyah (blood-money) amounts for specific wounds when they occur accidentally (khata). The full diyah is 100 camels (or equivalent). Mudihah (wound baring bone) incurs 1/20 of full diyah, i.e., 5 camels. Hashimah (fracturing bone) incurs 1/10, i.e., 10 camels. Munqilah (displacing bone) incurs 1/10 + 1/20 = 3/20, i.e., 15 camels. Ammah (wound exposing brain) and Ja'ifah (penetrating body cavity) each incur 1/3 of diyah. If a Ja'ifah penetrates through the body (creating two openings), it counts as two Ja'ifas and incurs 2/3 diyah. The commentator notes that these amounts apply when the wound is accidental; for intentional wounds, qisas (retaliation) may apply. The list is provided for memorization, as these are fixed legal amounts.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Blood-money; financial compensation paid to the victim or heirs for injury or death. Full diyah is 100 camels or equivalent.
خطاء (khata): Accidental; injury caused without intent. The text specifies that these diyah amounts apply when the wound is khata.
موضحہ (mudihah): Wound that bares the bone without causing fracture.
ہاشمہ (hashimah): Wound that fractures the bone but does not displace it.
منقلہ (munqilah): Wound that displaces the bone (fracture with displacement).
آمہ (ammah): Wound that reaches the brain membrane (exposes the brain).
جائفہ (ja'ifah): Wound that penetrates into a body cavity (chest, abdomen, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 1/20 of full diyah (5 camels)
B) 1/10 of full diyah (10 camels)
C) 1/10 + 1/20 of full diyah (15 camels)
D) 1/3 of full diyah (33.33 camels)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes fixed diyah fractions for six specific accidental wounds: mudihah (1/20), hashimah (1/10), munqilah (3/20), ammah (1/3), ja'ifah (1/3), and penetrating ja'ifah (2/3).

Ruling on Hukumat al-Adl for Wounds Below Mawdihah
Ruling on just assessment for wounds lacking fixed diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for wounds below mawdihah and explain why Hukumat al-Adl is wajib according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A wound below mawdihah has no fixed diyah or qisas; Hukumat al-Adl is wajib to honor human dignity.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi ruling for head wounds that do not expose the bone. Unlike mawdihah, these wounds have no fixed compensation, but Islamic law does not leave them unaddressed. The judge must assess a fair amount known as Hukumat al-Adl. The rationale is rooted in the principle that a believer's blood cannot be shed without just recompense.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wound type and determine the ruling
The passage specifies wounds below mawdihah (i.e., head or face wounds that do not expose the bone). For such wounds, qisas is not applicable, nor is there a fixed diyah. Instead, Hukumat al-Adl is wajib.
Mawdihah is the threshold; below it, no fixed compensation exists.
2
Understand the legal reasoning
Why no fixed diyah? The Lawgiver did not prescribe a specific amount for these minor wounds. Why not disregard? Because a Muslim's dignity demands compensation; ignoring the injury would violate this principle.
The reasoning is based on 'cannot be disregarded' and 'dignity of man'.
3
Analyze the transmitted evidence
The ruling is transmitted from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, indicating early practice. This qawl sahabi serves as a dalil for the Hanafi position.
The dalil is zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala in this context.
4
Clarify the Hanafi position and its authority
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, qisas is not applied for wounds below mawdihah. Therefore, Hukumat al-Adl is the only recourse. This is the mufta bihi position.
The authority weight is from the core Hanafi texts.
5
Note cross-madhhab differences
The ruling is mukhtalaf fih; other schools may apply qisas or fixed diyah for some intentional wounds below mawdihah. The Hanafi school uniquely holds Hukumat al-Adl.
Understanding the thamarah al-khilaf helps contextualize the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موضحہ سے کم میں حکومت عدل ہے
قال وفيما دون الموضحة حكومة العدل لانه ليس فيها ارش مقدرو لا يمكن اهداره فوجب اعتباره بحكم العدل وهو ماثور عن النخعى وعمر بن عبد العزيز .
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور مضحہ سے کم میں حکومت عدل ہے اس لئے کہ ان میں کوئی دیت مقرر نہیں ہے اور نہ اس کا اهدار ممکن ہے تو حکومت عدل کے ذریعہ اس کا اعتبار کرنا واجب ہوا ۔ اور یہی منقول ہے ابراہیم نخعی سے اور عمر بن عبد العزیز ہے۔ تشریح قدوری نے باقی میں فرمایا تھا کہ موضحہ کے علاوہ میں قصاص واجب نہیں ہے مگر ہم عرض کر چکے ہیں کہ صحیح روایت ظاہر الروایہ کی ہے۔ ( کما ) بہر حال جس روایت کے مطابق مادون الموضحہ میں قصاص واجب نہیں ہوا، تو اس میں حکومت عدل واجب ہے یعنی نہ دیت اور نہ قصاص ۔ عدم قصاص کی وجہ تو مذکور ہو چکی ہے، اور عدم دیت کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ شارع کی جانب سے تقدیر نہیں ہے اور اپنے قیاس سے ارش کی مقدار متعین نہیں کی جاسکتی۔ اور یہ بھی نہیں ہوسکتا کہ کچھ بھی واجب نہ ہو اور اس کو ہدر قرار دیا جائے۔ کیونکہ یہ تکریم انسان کے خلاف ہے تو جب کوئی چارہ نہ ملا تو ہم نے مجبوراً حکومت عدل کو اختیار کیا ہے اور یہ حضرت ابراہیم نخعی سے اور عمر بن عبد العزیز سے منقول ہے۔
For wounds less than mawdihah, there is Hukumat al-Adl. He said: And for wounds below mawdihah, Hukumat al-Adl is due, because there is no fixed diyah in it and it cannot be disregarded, so it is obligatory to consider it by just assessment, and it is transmitted from al-Nakha'i and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And for wounds less than mawdihah, Hukumat al-Adl is due, because there is no fixed diyah in them and it is not possible to disregard it, so it is obligatory to consider it through just assessment. And this is transmitted from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz. Commentary: Al-Quduri had stated previously that qisas is not obligatory for wounds other than mawdihah, but we have already submitted that the correct narration is that of Zahir al-Riwayah. In any case, according to the narration that qisas is not obligatory for wounds below mawdihah, then in such wounds Hukumat al-Adl is obligatory, meaning neither diyah nor qisas. The reason for the absence of qisas has already been mentioned, and the reason for the absence of diyah is that there is no determination from the Lawgiver, and the amount of compensation cannot be determined by one's own analogy. And it is also not possible that nothing be obligatory and it be considered disregarded, because this is against the dignity of man. So when there is no alternative, we have necessarily adopted Hukumat al-Adl. And this is transmitted from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage from the commentary of Al-Hidayah discusses the ruling for wounds less than mawdihah (bone-exposing head wound). Al-Quduri states that for such wounds, there is no fixed diyah (blood money) nor qisas (retaliation). Instead, the judge must assess a fair compensation called Hukumat al-Adl (just assessment). The reason is that the Lawgiver has not specified a fixed amount for these minor wounds, but they cannot be left uncompensated because human dignity requires recompense. The commentator notes that according to the sound narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), qisas is not applied, so Hukumat al-Adl is the only recourse. This position is transmitted from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (a prominent tabi'i) and Caliph Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz. The Hanafi school considers this ruling wajib (obligatory) because the alternative of leaving the injury uncompensated is unacceptable.

Key Terms
موضحہ (mawdihah): A wound on the head or face that lays bare the bone.
حکومت عدل (hukumat al-adl): Just assessment by a judge of compensation for wounds with no fixed diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What compensation is required for a wound on the head that does not expose the bone, according to the Hanafi school?
A) Qisas (retaliation)
B) Fixed diyah of 5 camels
C) Hukumat al-Adl (just assessment)
D) No compensation

Key Takeaway
For wounds below mawdihah, the Hanafi school mandates Hukumat al-Adl as obligatory compensation because no fixed amount exists, and leaving it uncompensated would violate human dignity.

Diyah Amounts for Accidental Head and Body Wounds
Specification of diyah fractions for accidental wounds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diyah fractions for mawdihah, hashimah, munqilah, ammah, and ja'ifah, and explain the evidence from the hadith of 'Amr ibn Hazm and the reasoning of Abu Bakr.

Core Idea
Diyah amounts are fixed by explicit Sunnah and analogical reasoning.

In the previous lesson, qisas for intentional wounds was discussed. Here, al-Quduri specifies the diyah (blood money) for these same wounds when they occur accidentally. The amounts are precise fractions of the full diyah, derived from the Prophet's decree and the ruling of Abu Bakr. We will examine each type, its diyah, and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wounds and their diyah fractions
List the five wound types: mawdihah (1/20 diyah), hashimah (1/10), munqilah (3/20), ammah (1/3), ja'ifah (1/3). Know the camel equivalents: 5, 10, 15, 33.33, 33.33.
Munqilah is 1/10 + 1/20 = 3/20.
2
Distinguish shijaj from ja'ifah
Shijaj are head/face wounds; ja'ifah penetrates a body cavity. Despite not being a shijaj, it is included here due to common occurrence.
The inclusion is incidental per al-Nihayah.
3
Examine the dalil from 'Amr ibn Hazm
The Prophet's written instruction specifies camel numbers for mawdihah, hashimah, munqilah, and ammah, and a separate hadith for ja'ifah.
The text is explicit and considered qat'i al-dalalah.
4
Understand the qiyas for penetrating ja'ifah
A nafidhah wound has two openings; each is treated as a separate ja'ifah, thus 2/3 diyah. This is supported by Abu Bakr's judgment.
Some object that it's one injury, but Hanafi response relies on precedent and analogy.
5
Recognize the authority of the proofs
The hadith and the ruling of Abu Bakr form the basis (zahir al-riwayah). The fractions are mufta bihi.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded for these amounts.

موضحہ اگر خطاء ہو تو دیت واجب ہے
قال وفى الموضحة ان كانت خطأ نصف عشر الدية وفى الهاشمة عشر الدية وفى المنقلة عشر الدية ونصف عشر الدية وفى الامة ثلث الدية وفى الجائفة ثلث الدية فان نفذت فهما جائفتان ففيهما ثلثا الدية
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور موضحہ میں اگر وہ خطا ہو دیت کے عشر کا نصف (یعنی بیسواں) ہے اور ہاشمہ میں دیت کا عشر ہے اور منقلہ میں دیت کا عشر اور دیت کا نصف عشر ہے اور آمہ میں تہائی دیت ہے اور جائفہ میں تہائی دیت ہے پس اگر جا ئفہ پار ہو جائے تو یہ دو جائفہیں ہیں پس ان دونوں میں دیت کا دو ثلث واجب ہو گا۔ تشریح ماقبل میں موضحہ کا حکم قصاص کا بیان کیا گیا ہے یہ اس وقت ہے جب کہ یہ زخم عمد لگایا گیا ہو اور اگر خطاء ہو تو اس میں دیت واجب ہوگی ۔ جن کی مقدار یہاں بیان کی گئی ہے اور اس کے علاوہ دیگر وہ زخم جن میں دیت واجب ہے وہاں خطاء کی قید ملحوظ نہیں ہے ؟
خطاء دونوں صورتوں میں یہی حکم ہے اب دیت کی تفصیل بیان فرماتے ہیں۔
- موضحہ میں، دیت کا بیسواں حصہ واجب ہوگا یعنی پانچ اونٹ۔
- ہاشمہ میں دیت کا عشر واجب ہوگا یعنی دس اونٹ ۔
- منقلہ میں عشر دیت اور نصف عشر واجب ہوگا یعنی پندرہ اونٹ ۔
- آمہ میں تہائی دیت واجب ہوگی۔
- جائفہ میں بھی تہائی دیت واجب ہوگی۔

سوال جائفہ کیا چیز ہے؟
جواب جائفہ وہ زخم ہے جو جوف تک پہنچ جائے ، خواہ سینہ میں ہو یا پیٹ میں یا کمر میں وغیرہ وغیرہ۔ سوال یہاں تو شجاج کا ذکر چل رہا ہے تو جائفہ کا ذکر کیوں آ گیا ؟ جواب صاحب نہایہ نے یہ کہا ہے کہ یہ ذکر یہاں اتفاقاً آ گیا ہے ورنہ شجاج فقط اس زخم کو کہتے ہیں جو سر اور چہرے میں ہوتا ہے۔ پھر فرمایا کہ جائفہ میں تہائی دیت جب واجب ہوگی، جب کہ وہ زخم پار نہ ہوا ہو۔ ورنہ اگر دوسری جانب پار ہو گیا تو پھر دیت سے دو ثلث واجب ہوں گے۔

مسئلہ مذکورہ کی دلیل
لماروى في كتاب عمرو بن حزم ان النبي عليه السلام قال وفى الموضحة خمس من الابل وفى الهاشمة عشر وفى المنقلة خمسة عشر وفى الامة ويروى المامومة ثلث الدية وقال عليه السلام في الجائفة ثلث الدية وعن ابى بكر انه حكم في جائفة نفذت الى الجانب الاخر بثلثى الدية ولا نها اذا نفذت نزلت منزلة جائفتين احدهما من جانب البطن والاخرى من جانب الظهر وفى كل جائفة ثلث الدية فلهذا وجب في النافذة ثلثا الدية
ترجمہ بوجہ اس کے کہ عمرو بن حزم کی کتاب میں مروی ہے کہ نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا اور موضحہ میں پانچ اونٹ ہیں اور ہاشمہ میں دس اونٹ ہیں اور منقلہ میں پندرہ اور آمہ میں، اور مروی ہے مامومہ میں تہائی دیت ہے اور نبی علیہ السلام نے فرمایا کہ جائفہ میں تہائی دیت ہے اور ابوبکر سے مروی ہے کہ انہوں نے اس جائفہ میں جو دوسری جانب پار ہو جائے دیت کے دو ثلث کا حکم فرمایا، اور اس لئے کہ جائفہ جب کہ پار ہو جائے تو اس کو دو جائفہ کے درجہ میں اتار لیا جائے گا ایک اندر کی جانب سے اور دوسرا باہر کی جانب سے اور ہر جائفہ میں تہائی دیت ہے اسی وجہ سے نافذ ( جو پار ہو جائے ) میں دو ثلث دیت ہو گی ۔
تشریح امام قدوری نے جو مسائل بیان فرمائے تھے ان تمام مسائل کے تین اجزاء ہیں تو دلیل کے بھی تعین جز ہیں۔ موضحہ میں پانچ اونٹ اور ہاشمہ میں دس اور منقلہ میں پندرہ اور آمہ میں تہائی دیت اس کی دلیل میں عمرو بن حزم کی کتاب کی پہلی حدیث بیان فرمائی۔
جائفہ میں ثلث دیت ہے اس کے ثبوت میں دوسری حدیث پیش فرمائی۔
- اگر جا ئفہ ایک جانب پار ہو جائے تو اس کے ثبوت میں حضرت صدیق اکبر کا فیصلہ پیش فرمایا ہے۔
دوسری دلیل عقلی پیش فرمائی کہ جب جا ئفہ پار ہو گیا تو اب وہ ایک جائفہ نہیں رہا بلکہ دو ہوگئے اور ہر جائفہ میں تہائی دیت واجب ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا دو میں دو ثلث واجب ہوگی۔
If the mawdihah is accidental, then diyah is wajib. He said: And in mawdihah, if it is accidental, half of a tenth of the diyah; and in hashimah, a tenth of the diyah; and in munqilah, a tenth and a half-tenth of the diyah; and in ammah, a third of the diyah; and in ja'ifah, a third of the diyah. Then if it penetrates, then they are two ja'ifahs, so in them two-thirds of the diyah. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And in mawdihah, if it is accidental, half of a tenth of the diyah (i.e., one-twentieth) is due; and in hashimah, a tenth of the diyah; and in munqilah, a tenth and a half-tenth of the diyah; and in ammah, a third of the diyah; and in ja'ifah, a third of the diyah. Then if the ja'ifah penetrates through, then there are two ja'ifahs, so in them two-thirds of the diyah are wajib. Commentary: Previously, the ruling of qisas for mawdihah was mentioned; that is when the wound was inflicted intentionally. If it is accidental, then diyah is wajib. The amounts are stated here. And other wounds in which diyah is wajib? The condition of accidental is not observed? In both cases of accidental, this ruling applies. Now he details the diyah: - In mawdihah, one-twentieth of diyah is wajib, meaning five camels. - In hashimah, one-tenth of diyah is wajib, meaning ten camels. - In munqilah, one-tenth and half-tenth of diyah is wajib, meaning fifteen camels. - In ammah, one-third of diyah is wajib. - In ja'ifah also, one-third of diyah is wajib. Question: What is ja'ifah? Answer: Ja'ifah is the wound that reaches the body cavity, be it in the chest, belly, or back, etc. Question: Here the discussion is about shijaj (head wounds), so why is ja'ifah mentioned? Answer: The author of al-Nihayah said that it came here incidentally; otherwise shijaj are only wounds to the head and face. Then he said that one-third of diyah is wajib in ja'ifah when it has not penetrated. Otherwise, if it penetrates to the other side, then two-thirds of diyah are wajib. Proof of the mentioned ruling: Because it is narrated in the book of 'Amr ibn Hazm that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: And in mawdihah, five camels; and in hashimah, ten; and in munqilah, fifteen; and in ammah (it is also narrated as ma'mumah), a third of diyah; and he (peace be upon him) said: In ja'ifah, a third of diyah. And it is narrated from Abu Bakr that he judged in a ja'ifah that penetrated to the other side: two-thirds of diyah. And because when it penetrates, it is considered as two ja'ifahs: one from the side of the belly and the other from the side of the back, and in each ja'ifah there is a third of diyah, so for this reason, two-thirds of diyah are due in the penetrating wound. Translation: Because it is narrated in the book of 'Amr ibn Hazm that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: And in mawdihah, five camels; and in hashimah, ten camels; and in munqilah, fifteen; and in ammah (and it is narrated ma'mumah): a third of the diyah; and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: In ja'ifah, a third of the diyah. And it is narrated from Abu Bakr that he judged in a ja'ifah that penetrated to the other side: two-thirds of the diyah. And because when a ja'ifah penetrates, it is considered as two ja'ifahs: one from the inner side and the other from the outer side, and in each ja'ifah there is a third of diyah, therefore in the penetrating wound (nafidhah), two-thirds of diyah are due. Commentary: The rulings that Imam al-Quduri mentioned have three parts, so the proof also has three parts. For mawdihah, hashimah, munqilah, and ammah, the proof is the first hadith from the book of 'Amr ibn Hazm. For ja'ifah, the second hadith is presented. For the penetrating ja'ifah, the proof is the judgment of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him). A second rational proof: when the ja'ifah penetrates, it is no longer one ja'ifah but two, and each ja'ifah requires one-third of diyah, so two-thirds become wajib.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage details the diyah (blood money) amounts for specific wounds when they occur accidentally (khatā'). Al-Quduri lists the fractions as established by the Sunnah: mawdihah (bone-exposing head wound) gets 1/20 of full diyah (5 camels), hashimah (fracture) gets 1/10 (10 camels), munqilah (displaced bone) gets 3/20 (15 camels), ammah (brain-reaching wound) gets 1/3, and ja'ifah (wound penetrating the body cavity) gets 1/3. If the ja'ifah goes through and through, it counts as two wounds, so 2/3 diyah. The commentator defines ja'ifah and explains why it is mentioned here (though it is a body wound, not a head wound). The proofs come from the famous letter of 'Amr ibn Hazm containing the Prophet's (saw) decrees, and from the judgment of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq on a penetrating wound. Additionally, a rational analogy (qiyas) is given: a penetrating wound creates two openings, each considered a separate ja'ifah, thus 1/3+1/3=2/3. This is the established Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
شجاج (shijaj): Wounds specific to the head and face.
ہاشمہ (hashimah): A fracture of the skull without displacement.
منقلہ (munqilah): A fracture where bone is displaced, requiring surgical intervention.
آمہ (ammah (or ma'mumah)): A wound reaching the brain membrane (umm al-dimagh).
جائفہ (ja'ifah): Any wound that penetrates into a body cavity (chest, abdomen, back).
نافذہ (nafidhah): A penetrating wound that goes through the body, exiting from the other side.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the diyah amount for ammah (brain-reaching wound) in the Hanafi school when accidental?
A) 1/10 of full diyah (10 camels)
B) 1/20 of full diyah (5 camels)
C) 1/3 of full diyah (33.33 camels)
D) 2/3 of full diyah (66.66 camels)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses precise fractions of diyah for each accidental head and body wound, derived from prophetic decree and the judgment of Abu Bakr.
